Back in the day, whenever the Nine Wisemen went on an adventure, fought a battle, or made public appearances, Meilin would always wear a monk robe and fox themed half mask, so her face was not known to the common people.

But other players, especially those in high positions in other countries or highly skilled, had met her in person and knew what she looked like.

“I can tell you’re faintly aware of this, given the fake name you gave, but…”

Mira did not take a break, continuing to reprimand Meilin’s carelessness, while making sure she understood the situation. Meilin had been really lucky that she had not run into anyone who recognized her yet, as otherwise it could cause a big international issue.

“I’m sure you understand luck isn’t going to save you this time, yes? This tournament is a really big deal, and the best combatants from every country are taking part. So there’s plenty of people in this city that can recognize you…”

She continued to explain how dangerous it could be if Meilin’s identity became widespread, just like Solomon had explained it before. It was only a matter of time before reports of Meilin sightings all over the continent would come rushing in, putting all of Arkite in a difficult position.

“I don’t want to cause Solomon any trouble… But I want to fight…”

The Nine Wisemen were the leading military force of Arkite, so seeing one of them wandering unannounced through other countries could lead to a lot of suspicion being cast on the country, especially as they were still in a ceasefire.

Meilin understood the circumstances and lowered her face, looking dejected as she mumbled to Mira. Even if she understood the dangers, she had been really looking forward to the tournament, and found it hard to let go.

“Well, I have a suggestion about that.”

Seeing Meilin’s reaction, Mira put some more energy in her voice as she revealed her plan. Put simply, they simply had to make it impossible to tie her to the Nine Wisemen.

“That’s why we prepared this entire disguise for you. I’ll give it to you if you promise to return to Arkite afterward. Solomon also said you can take part in the tournament if you wear it.”

The disguise was the hair dye, the Magical Girl getup prepared by Lily and the maids, and a special choker to deter photographs, which would let out a particular type of mana that made it impossible for lenses to focus on the wearer’s face.

“Okay! I promise! Please let me fight in the tournament!”

She made a full recovery from her dejected state. That was exactly what Solomon had anticipated would happen if Meilin was first told she could not participate, and then given a way out, either because he knew how to manipulate others, or because Meilin’s personality was so straightforward. Regardless, she had happily promised to return and to wear the disguise, so Mira triumphantly told her, “Then I’ll grant you this disguise.”

Now that Meilin had promised to go back to Arkite, Mira had fulfilled half her mission. All that was left to do was to make sure Meilin would not get recognized.

So Mira quickly told Meilin to put on the disguise, starting with the hair dye, which would turn her dark blue hair into a bright red.

“Hmm…that’s about it, I’d say.”

Meilin was obediently going along with everything, as she really wanted to take part in the tournament. That made it easy for Mira to apply the hair dye, and now she nodded satisfied at the result.

Mira had gotten a good idea of how to do it after watching Theresa the day before, and she had done a decent job at it. The color was largely uniform, although there was a slight darkening in some areas. But at a quick glance, it looked like raging flames, so Mira decided to call it a lucky coincidence, since she thought it looked pretty cool.

“That’s incredible! It’s all so red!”

When they were done, Meilin also ran up to a mirror to look at herself, amazed at how different her hair looked. She also noticed the variation in color, which made her say, “That’s so cool, it’s like I’m on fire!”

“I know, I know! That’s what I was going for!”

Meilin seemed to like that, and Mira acted like that had been her plan all along. Then Mira made Meilin sit down again to apply the conditioner which would preserve the dyed color for longer. And with that, the first step of the disguise was complete.

With her hair done, it was time to put on the new clothes, the special Magical Girl outfit carefully crafted by Lily and the maids.

“Grandfather…I don’t understand these clothes…” Meilin went to put them on, and only a few seconds later was already asking for help.

“Hm? What is it?”

Mira was looking away while Meilin changed, but turned around since otherwise she would not be able to help. Once she checked out the issue, she let out a, “Oh no…” while frowning, and then sighing as she silently cursed the maids for going overboard again.

Back when they handed the outfit to Mira, she had not asked what it was supposed to look like or anything like that. It was a disguise for Meilin so she did not really care, or rather, it was not her issue.

At the same time, she had already been subjected to so much by Lily and the maids that she felt confident she could figure out clothes, but that confidence was her downfall. Mira had only glimpsed at a fraction of the world of fashion, and only realized that truth now.

Meilin’s disguise was far more complicated than any dress Mira had ever laid her eyes on.

It was a mishmash of colors, a short and very revealing skirt paired with a pink petticoat. And all of that was covered in a jumble of cute frills and lace.

“Hmmm, I can’t figure this out either… Wait a bit.”

On top of being so unexpectedly complex, there was an almost ridiculous number of additional pieces of cloth, and it was impossible to figure out what went where. Mira deemed it a lost cause herself, and rushed out to seek Vanessa’s help to rescue them.

“Woahh, it’s all done! You look so cute, Meimei!”

Ten odd minutes later, Meilin succeeded in wearing the whole disguise, thanks to the aid provided by Vanessa, and the reference sheets that Vanessa had found.

When she arrived, she said that a dress that complicated should have a diagram showing what it was meant to look like, so she searched the bag that the dress came in, and found those reference sheets. After that, it was just a matter of following the drawings and getting Meilin all dressed up like a brand new fighting Magical Girl.

“I can’t believe it! It’s like I’ve become someone else!”

Meilin stood in front of the mirror, looking at her complete disguise with joy and surprise. Then she added, “I look like a PrePure!” echoing the same thought Mira had.

Put simply, the overall design of the disguise was very reminiscent of the heroines from an anime series aimed at young girls, which had also become really popular amongst adults. And it even looked like the powered up form introduced halfway through the series.

(I get it now…it’s all because of him.)

They were supposed to make a disguise, not a whole transformation. But now a new PrePure had just been born out of nowhere, and Mira had a pretty good idea of who was responsible for that.

The main suspect was Lastrada. Being a big fan of superheroes and justice, each Sunday morning was a sacred time for him, as TV series featuring them would be broadcast at that time.

PrePure was also a series filled with justice and broadcasted at that time. So Lastrada became a fan of them as well.

Then, when the plan of making a disguise for Meilin came up, Solomon decided to bring in Lastrada as a consultant to ensure it would be a success, since he already had experience with disguises.

In the end, he influenced Lily and the maids to create the disguise for his ideal heroine.

(That’s so dirty…)

Instead of disguising Meilin, they had transformed them at their whim. Mira had many conflicting feelings about that, but seeing Meilin in that attire was enough to know that no one would recognize her.

A PrePure-like Magical Girl was the polar opposite to the martial arts obsessed girl Meilin was known as, and the hair color change on top of that completed the PrePure look. The path there might have been twisted, but the results were undeniable.

“Since it’s come to this, why don’t you try striking a few poses too?”

When Mira suggested that, Meilin immediately said, “That sounds fun!” and began trying out various poses. Growing up, she had also been a big PrePure fan, so she still had plenty of poses and even catchphrases perfectly memorized.

Watching that, Mira’s thoughts went to the tournament again, and how the public would react to her.

There was no way of concealing Meilin’s strength in the tournament, and the audience would take note of that. She would still stand out a lot as a PrePure, a mysterious heroine of justice, but all of that attention would actually distract from her identity as a Wiseman.

There was not a single person who would ever associate PrePure with Meilin. Mira herself noticed that, as she had to constantly remind herself that it really was Meilin standing in front of the mirror.

“Umm…What is PrePure?”

Eventually, Vanessa asked that, thoroughly puzzled by Meilin’s catchphrases and poses. All Mira could say in response was, “PrePure is a legendary warrior of another land.”

Mira also happened to know a thing or two about PrePure, but that was because she had spent a lot of time playing with her younger sister, and also watched TV with her.

After getting over the surprise of having turned into a PrePure, which Meilin liked quite a lot, she began testing her new outfit’s mobility.

Then again, she was one of the Nine Wisemen, so even her practice movements were sharp and precise, making quick swishing sounds as her limbs cut through the air one after another.

“It doesn’t get in the way at all! It’s perfect!”

She announced her opinion after one round of practice movements. The handiwork of Lily and the maids had received the seal of approval from Meilin as well.

Mira nodded with satisfaction seeing how happy Meilin was, and a moment later was startled by a knock on the door.

“Mira, Meimei, would you like to have dinner with us?”

It was Henry’s voice. His invitation was rather straightforward, but there was a strange tumult behind him, so someone else had to be with him.

“I’m always down for dinner!”

Meilin was the first one to reply, instantly opening the door after hearing the word dinner, revealing Henry standing there together with all of his siblings.

At the same time the children shouted, “Now!” and brought out wooden swords to swing at Meilin. It seemed like they also had that common challenge of pupils trying to land at least one hit on their master.

But their swings never completed, as the children retreated in shock and confusion, their eyes locked on Meilin…the Legendary Warrior PrePure.

“Huh…? Where’s Meimei?”

“Who…who are you?”

It was all because of the disguise. It was so perfect that no one realized it was her.

In response, Meilin just struck each of their heads with a hand chop, giggling as she said, “You still need to train more.”

“Huhhh?! You’re Meimei?!”

“For real??”

The children were still struggling to understand that. Her voice and actions were the same as the Meimei they knew, but she looked completely different. And Meilin decided to stand proud as she spoke to them.

“Meimei is just my alter ego to move in this world. I’m actually the Legendary Warrior PrePure!”

While it was a bit strange for a superhero to reveal their identity so openly, at least Meilin had really gotten into character with her disguise. The children, still of a tender age, swallowed everything she said too. They had no idea what the Legendary Warrior PrePure was, but they did not care either, it sounded cool and that was enough for them.

“Keep this a secret, okay?”

All of the children agreed in unison. Then after a few seconds they tried to charge at her again.

“Still not enough!”

In one swift motion, Meilin swept off everyone’s feet, her dress following her movements elegantly like a true PrePure.

“By the way, she’s going to participate in the tournament looking like that now. Is it still possible to amend her application form?”

While Meilin played with the children, Mira went to talk with Henry. ‘Meimei’ was still too obvious for a fake name, so Mira wanted to amend the form with a more appropriate name.

“So she’ll be the Legendary Warrior uh…Pre…Pure…was it? Well, that shouldn’t be much of an issue.”

Henry barely had to think about it, despite it being a whole title and not just a different name. He then explained that they had already received many applications with strange names, like Snowwhite Princess or Midnight Cavalier. Those tended to be nobles who wanted to test their skills without bringing attention to their families, or just popular personages who were there for fun. The Legendary Warrior PrePure would fit in amongst them without issue.

“I still can hardly believe that’s her though… But I’m curious, was this the reason why you were looking for Meimei?”

Henry muttered that as he took another look at Meilin’s new appearance. It was easy to connect the dots, as the transformation happened as soon as Mira and Meilin got a moment alone.

“Yes, that’s correct.”

Meilin would likely remain in Henry’s care for a while longer, so Mira felt the need to share a few things with him just in case, which boiled down to explaining that Meilin was someone in a rather high position, and that it was best for her to not stand out too much in public.

“I see… So she was here undercover the whole time. I had a hunch that could be the case, judging by her skills.”

It was hard to know just how much Henry had already deduced. He just smiled a bit and did not pry any further.

(Alright… It’s pretty much safe to say that my mission is complete now!)

Mira had done everything she could. At this point, the only identifying factor was that Meilin was a Sage, and that was something Mira would never take away from her. Everyone in that tournament was competing to be the strongest, so trying to fight without one’s main abilities would be self-sabotage, and would invalidate any reason to take part in the tournament.

Mira already knew what it was like to be denied something like that, as she herself was banned from taking part. So she abstained from saying anything more to Meilin.

If for whatever reason Meilin’s identity was still uncovered, it would be something completely unavoidable, and Mira could wash her hands from it.

+++

# **327: Wind-down Time**

Everyone gathered around the table to share a delightful dinner, after which it was time to take a bath. But before that, Henry and his siblings headed to the training area, as they claimed that a knight’s duty was also to be able to move and act even if it was right after eating.

That did not apply to Meilin though.

“I already took a bath yesterday, so I’m fine. Don’t worry.”

“No no, that won’t do. That was yesterday, and today is today.”

She was currently arguing with Vanessa.

Meilin had always hated taking baths, while Vanessa would not allow that, especially after her usual training coupled with the violent fight with Mira. Vanessa found it outrageous to not take a bath after all that, and was insistent on keeping the house guest in a presentable condition.

“Then I’ll take one tomorrow. That’ll be even better.”

Not even Meilin believed the words out of her mouth as she attempted to run away, only to find her escape blocked by a Holy Knight’s shield.

Seeing the unexpected obstacle made Meilin take a quick evasive maneuver, which also happened to be her downfall as Vanessa jumped in to take hold of her, after which other maids also gathered to restrain her and take her away.

“That was mean! You traitor!!”

The maids carried Meilin off to the bathroom as she shouted with indignation, and Mira just watched that while pretending not knowing what she was talking about. But then it was Mira’s turn.

“Thank you for your assistance, Lady Mira. Allow me to accompany you to the bathroom as well.”

Vanessa also wanted to take Mira there.

That made her freeze in place. Usually, Mira would have happily obliged and taken a bath with all the maids, except for one factor that was different here.

It was Meilin, a girl who knew Mira’s true identity. Then again, considering her usual behavior, Meilin would not think much of taking a bath together. The main issue was how loose her mouth tended to be.

It was only a matter of time before Meilin would bring up how gleefully Mira took a bath with her and the maids, and if someone like Kagura happened to be present, she would forever look at Mira with disgust.

“No, I just…”

At the same time, it was a bit late to start worrying about such things. Still, Mira wanted to cling to her past dignity and began to stammer, which Vanessa noticed.

“Or…could it be that you also detest baths, Lady Mira…?”

Vanessa cared for her guests wholeheartedly and would not allow them to remain in an unwashed state. In response, Mira rapidly shook her head, “No no no, that’s not it, I love taking baths!” and tried to find a way out.

“It’s just…right, the garden. I’m still a bit worried about it. We had to mend it in a hurry, remember? I’d like to go see how it’s holding up so far, but then I might get dirty again being there, so I figured I’d wait until later to take a bath.”

She rapidly mouthed off the first excuse that occurred to her, and it seemed like focusing on the garden made it especially effective, as Vanessa’s stern gaze softened.

“In that case, I’ll go with you too!”

Or rather, it ended up being too effective, as Vanessa was the main maid in charge of the garden, and she also wanted to see how it was doing.

“Oh, you don’t have to…or rather, you know, I might end up using some secret summon…”

Special abilities kept secret were common in this world, not just amongst spellcasters. Even the Adams Family had a few passed down through their lineage. And as a servant of the Adams Residence, Vanessa was well aware of that, and rescinded as soon as Mira hinted at it.

“If that’s the case…I understand.”

She turned around, looking a bit disappointed, and headed to the bathroom instead.

Once she was gone, Mira let out a sigh of relief, and then headed out to the garden, to give at least some credibility to her excuse.

(Hmmm… Maybe I should’ve gone on the offensive instead when that happened…)

She gave the lawn and plants a cursory glance, as she had claimed she would do, and then switched gears to review her fight with Meilin, thinking back to the abilities she used, the timing of her summons, as well as the general tactics she used and the alternatives that could have been more effective.

The fight itself had provided plenty of information, as expected from a formidable opponent like Meilin. Mira had been able to try out various new abilities and tactics, and get clear results on how effective they were, and what she could improve. There were also plenty of other things she wanted to test in the future.

She continued thinking about random things like that as she wandered around the garden.

“It’s Miraaaaaaa!”

“Come with us, we’ll take a bath together!”

Then suddenly, loud voices came from the training area, as four small shadows scurried out into the garden. They were the kids who had just finished their post-dinner training and were heading to take a bath, which was when they spotted Mira and tried to bring her along.

“Hey hey, don’t pull on me like that, I’ll go, okay?”

Cinthia and Rosemary clung onto Mira’s arms and began tugging on her. Meanwhile, the boys Ryan and Fabian were looking at her with starry eyes, begging her to tell them stories of her adventures while they took a bath.

Henry and his parents were a distance away, looking at her apologetically, but also lowering their head slightly, entrusting her with the kids. By then, there was no way for Mira to back out.

By the time Mira got there, Meilin and the maids had already finished bathing, as they were nowhere to be seen. She was slightly disappointed by that, as she even had the perfect excuse of saying she just wanted to watch after the kids. But then she looked around and nodded in approval, saying, “Now this is good!” being impressed by the bath that looked straight out of a hot spring resort.

It really was a magnificent bathroom, which made sense for the mansion of a noble family. And then her admiration was interrupted by the excited voices of children. Despite the nice bathroom, she would not get to enjoy it calmly.

(Somehow, I feel like I keep ending up having to watch over kids lately…)

Regardless of those thoughts, she still took care of them, and once they all settled down, the third son Fabian began insisting on hearing about Mira’s adventures, the places she had visited, or dungeons she went through. She obliged, telling them about the Forest of Praying Children, the Abandoned City in the Sky, the Libra Fortress, the Ancient Underground City, and so on, eventually getting carried away and even telling them things that happened back when she was still Danbulf.

“That’s so cool! I also want to go to a bunch of dungeons when I become an adventurer like you!”

Fabian was deeply inspired by all those stories, dreaming about experiencing similar adventures himself. He already pictured himself becoming a world class adventurer, finding a legendary treasure, then buying a flying ship to go on even more adventures around the world.

“That’s splendid. Then the first step will be becoming stronger, so you can not only protect your companions, but yourself as well.”

Children had nearly endless potential for their futures, and Mira reaffirmed that as she patted Fabian’s head. He replied with a bright smile while saying, “Yes, I’ll become really strong!” showing he was also confident he could attain the future he dreamed of so dearly.

Next to him was Ryan, who looked rather pensive. his eyes locked on Mira as he thought, _“I guess strong men are always better.”_

“Umm umm…you were also in the fight against Chimera Clauzen, right? Does that mean…did you get to meet Jack Grave there?!”

When Mira was largely done telling her stories, the eldest sister Cinthia asked that. She was still young, but her eyes were already full of admiration.

But it was not admiration for Mira. It was obvious she had the heart of a maiden, and she only had eyes for Jack Grave.

“Hmm… Ohh, yes, I have met him.”

That name did not ring any bells at all, but Mira decided to pretend she knew who he was. Cinthia made it seem like he had also participated in that fight, and that he was a famous adventurer of sorts.

With all of that in mind, Mira delved deeper into her memories, trying to remember all the famous adventurers she met back then. The first one that sprung out to her was that sexy woman, Eleonora. She had a really striking appearance that was still burned into Mira’s memories.

That refreshed the scene at the time, and Mira realized Eleonora had also introduced her to another famous person, whose name definitely sounded something like Jack Grave.

Now that she had recalled that, she had nothing to be afraid of, so she added with a pompous voice, “He was with me on the flying ship when we made our victory announcement.”

“That’s incredible! You actually met him, you met Jack Grave! And you were together on a flying ship…! I’m so jealous!”

Cinthia did not notice that Mira had forgotten so much, instead growing more excited hearing the response.

“You got to see him from so close! What kind of man was he?! He was really dashing and courageous, right?!”

She was deeply passionate about Jack Grave, as she hounded Mira with more questions, really expectant of Mira’s replies.

Mira had an internal conflict, mostly because she could not even remember his face very clearly. Not to mention that for her, a dashing and courageous man was closer to her previous appearance, or someone like Arlon who had recently become an instructor in Arkite, basically someone with a more mature and aged appearance, full of dandyism.

On the other hand, Jack Grave was that while strong, he was handsome with a more youthful charm, and what she could remember the most clearly were the shrill cheers that came from the audience when he showed up.

In other words, he was far too young when compared to Mira’s ideals, and despite her envy for his popularity, he did not appear dashing or courageous in Mira’s eyes.

“Hmm, well yes, he was dashing and courageous. He was really shining that day.”

In the end, that was her reply. She knew that this was not the moment to express her own opinion, and that the right answer was to validate Cinthia’s emotions instead.

“So you also thought that! He’s so cool, Jack Grave the One Hit Dragon Slayer!”

Cinthia was excited, believing she had found a kindred soul, speaking with a dreamlike voice, “One day I’ll also meet Jack Grave and join his guild.”

It did not seem like she was going to wake up to reality any time soon. While that happened, the second daughter Rosemary began to mumble in a low voice, eventually the words, “I…Sero…” ringing clear through her embarrassment.

And that stuck out clearly to Mira.

“Ohh, you like Sero? He really is an impressive man, you’ve got good taste.”

Thanks to all her recent experiences, Mira had learned that wherever there were loud kids, there were also quieter ones, and she knew it was important to also listen to them before their voices were drowned out by everyone else. Not to mention that, this time, it was easier as a name she was well acquainted with had been brought up.

Sero was the leader of a guild called Écarlate Carillon, and was a surprisingly softhearted man despite his top notch skills. His guild was also blessed with wonderful comrades (excluding Fricca), overall making him a great man.

“Mhm, Sero is amazing.”

Rosemary had been nervous and hesitant thus far, but she looked up with joy when Mira recognized Sero, almost like it had been about herself. Then, driven by the joy of having found common ground, she slowly moved the conversation along.

She began mentioning what she liked about Sero, which were her favorite stories about him, and overall showing she was just as passionate about Sero like Cinthia was about Jack Grave.

“I heard Sero was also there in the fight with Chimera Clauzen, but no one knows anything else. Do you know about that?”

After her initial burst of fervor, Rosemary asked her first real question. She basically wanted to know where and how Sero fought against Chimera Clauzen.

By now, many of the stories from that fight had already spread, mostly through the mouths of those present. There had been many other adventurers fighting alongside Jack Grave and Eleonora, so those stories had spread quite a bit.

But no one seemed to know about Sero, other than him being there.

There was one big reason for that. He had been fighting the higherups of Chimera Clauzen separated from the rest, alongside Mira and Kagura. And they were the only ones who knew what had happened there.

Kagura still kept herself secret from the public, and Sero was not the type to sing his own praises. Which meant that there was no source for the stories of that fight to spread.

“Yes, I know. In fact, he was fighting right alongside me!”

As soon as those words left Mira’s mouth, Rosemary looked at her with visible excitement.

No one knew about the fight with Chimera Clauzen’s higher-ups, not because it was kept secret, but because those involved were not the type to talk. Now one of them was there, and willing to tell the story, all to fulfill the wishes of a dreaming girl.

“…And we were in charge of their top brass. So we had to chase after the remaining ones after that.”

Mira began telling the story of how they stormed Chimera Clauzen’s headquarters, continuing until they chased after the remaining higher-ups, at which point they split up to continue fighting individually. Mira did not know who Sero fought after that, so instead she told her own story, making sure to stress just how important her summons had been. Then when the fight was over, they regrouped and flew on Pegasus to return to the base where the rest of their allies were waiting.

“Incredible! You’re all so strong!”

“Aww… I could’ve heard more about Jack Grave if he also fought alongside you…”

Fabian was simply excited by the story. Cinthia was filled with envy, wishing she could also hear first hand accounts of Jack Grave’s exploits. And Rosemary…

“Flying with Sero on Pegasus…I didn’t think of that…!”

She looked like she had received a revelation, thinking of various possibilities to get closer to him, or be of some help to him, or just something…

At least she did not seem to mind that Mira had been so close to Sero in the past.

The way Mira spoke made it clear that there was nothing else between the two, or maybe it was just her female intuition telling her that.

Which was something Ryan lacked entirely, as he was completely silent, his heart beating painfully fast.

He had just heard Mira refer to another man, Jack Grave, as dashing and courageous. Then she doubled down by talking about Sero, who she called impressive.

Soon after, Fabian pushed Mira to tell them more about her adventures in the Ancient Underground City, while Ryan continued to think that he needed to be strong enough to defeat a dragon, or charismatic enough to lead a large and well known guild, before he would be seen as a man by Mira.

+++

# **328: The Imperial Chambers**

Meilin’s footsteps had led Mira to visit the Adams Residence, finally allowing her to meet with Meilin and accomplish her mission. After that, Mira spent the night there as well.

The next morning, she was invited to a lavish breakfast, and then she went to train with the children and Meilin.

They got a bit carried away again, but at least the garden remained safe this time.

After their usual morning routine, it was time for Henry to head to work in the palace, and Mira went along with him.

She had already ensured Meilin had her disguise and had dyed her hair, so she should be safe for the moment. Mira had also briefed Vanessa on various things, essentially telling her that despite her appearance, Meilin was an undercover idol of sorts, so Mira trusted that Vanessa would take care of everything else.

The actual preliminaries and the following main tournament would be the main issue either way, as an enormous audience would have their eyes on Meilin, and the disguise would be the most important.

“Thank you for looking after my siblings. I can’t remember the last time they were so motivated to train.”

“No need to thank me, I’m quite fond of children myself, and I enjoyed my time with them. Actually, could I see them again if I come to visit my friend?”

“But of course, I’m sure they’d be delighted to see you too. If anything I hope you can come see us again.”

Henry’s siblings had been a joy to be around, but they had also grown attached to Mira despite only knowing each other for one day, so leaving the Adams Residence had been quite the ordeal.

After that, the two chatted about other random things as they walked through the city.

Henry’s workplace, the palace, was roughly a kilometer away from the Adams Residence, and he always chose to walk there instead of taking a carriage so he could keep watch of the city. That decision made him quite well known amongst the residents living around the palace.

“Ah, good morning Sir Henry.”

“Good morning, Sir Henry. Please come share a drink with us again sometime.”

People constantly greeted him, like a passing carriage coach or a nearby barkeeper. Henry smiled and greeted all of them back too.

They were really friendly interactions despite him being a noble, and the mutual respect was also clear. It was an exemplary show of the ideal relationship between nobles and citizens, either because of how the country was led, or just Henry’s personality. Either way, Mira was impressed to see those interactions.

It did not take long before they also noticed that Mira was with him, and for someone to mention it.

“Aww, and that cute girl? Could she be…”

An older lady, the type who loved to gossip, looked at Mira as she raised her voice. A certain thought flashed in Mira’s mind instantly, thinking of the interaction that would follow right after.

‘Could she be your girlfriend?’, ‘What?! No, that’s not it’, ‘Oh you little rascal, don’t play dumb after pulling such a cutie.’

That was a really common trope in romance stories, after which the protagonist and heroine would blush and look at each other.

She had never expected that she would end up being in that position, even less in the role of the heroine.

All of those thoughts went by in an instant in Mira’s mind, and then the old lady finished her sentence.

“…a lost child? It’s still pretty early to be getting lost. Maybe she got split from her parents while doing an early market run?”

It was something completely different from what Mira had anticipated, completely stunning her as she froze with her eyes wide open. She had been so confident in her own looks that it would not surprise her to be mistaken for Henry’s partner, only for things to go in pretty much the opposite direction.

“I’ve never seen her around here before. She might have come to watch the tournament with her family and then got lost when leaving the event area.”

While Mira remained stunlocked from the unexpected reaction, a passing elderly man joined in, looking worried for Mira. Then they began asking what her parents’ names were, what she was called, where she was staying, and so on. It did not take long before a sizable group of people gathered around her, all with gentle smiles volunteering to go search for her parents.

And then it finally was enough.

“No, listen, she’s actually…”

Henry had also been overwhelmed by the overzealous people, and finally was able to get a word in and explain the situation.

Now it was his duty to turn the misunderstanding around, and show that the girl everyone thought was a lost child, was actually an amazing adventurer they should respect. Mira fell silent, letting him do all the work, praying that he would be convincing enough while looking at the crowd around her to see how they would react.

In the end, Henry succeeded in cleansing Mira from being branded a lost child, but as the crowd was mainly composed of older people who did not know much about adventurers, they did not show much of a reaction to the name of Spirit Queen.

With all of that dealt with, Mira and Henry resumed their walk to the palace, arriving there not too long after.

“This is where we part ways then. Feel free to visit us whenever you want, I’m sure my siblings will appreciate it.”

“Yes, I’ll try to drop by again soon enough.”

The two exchanged those words in front of the imperial chambers of Nirvana’s Imperial Palace. After that Henry returned to his post, and Mira went through the doors into the imperial chambers.

Mira’s mission was halfway done now. The only thing left was to make sure Meilin was properly disguised once the tournament started.

With that weight off her shoulders, Mira was ready to be briefed on the details of her mission to watch over the oracle, which was also important.

“I’ll be done in ten…fifteen minutes. Just wait for me inside.”

“Hm, alright.”

Once inside, she found Alma once again buried under a pile of paperwork, which had only grown taller with all the arrangements for the tournament.

Some of her work needed to be done within that morning, so she was going to be busy for a bit longer before they could discuss the mission properly. Until then, Mira was given access to the room further inside.

The imperial chambers included Alma’s office, which was surrounded with bookshelves packed with books and files, with one wall having Nirvana’s flag and those of its allies on display, including Arkite’s which Mira was very familiar with.

Then there was a door leading further inside, where Mira was told to wait. She reached for the doorknob without thinking much of it, when Alma behind her added, “Ah, and feel free to reach into the fridge.”

“Ohh, got it!”

Hearing that, she pushed forward without reserve, and once in the next room she let out a loud, “Woahh…” in admiration.

While the office had been furnished with a focus on getting work done, the room past the door looked like the VIP room of a first class hotel, filled with all sorts of luxuries.

The table, chairs, and sofa were all of high quality, while the cupboard was filled with all sorts of delicacies. The various appliances there like the fridge, lights, and even air conditioning also looked far more expensive than those found in most households.

In short, it was a room furnished in a way befit of the empress.

“So she actually has a proper room like this too.”

The previous day, Alma had received Mira in her private room, which appeared almost meagre in comparison. Here there was a proper bathroom, a toilet, and an elegant and vast kitchen, allowing one to cook even the most complex dishes.

All of that belonged to Alma as well, but it did not have many signs of use, showing that Alma preferred to sleep and spend her free time in the smaller private room.

“Well, it’s not like I don’t understand that feeling.”

As much as living in luxury was desirable, it could get exhausting to be in such an environment everyday. Mira had grown up amongst common people, so she also understood that feeling. But experiencing it from time to time was the best, and easily the most obvious luxury was food.

Mira made a beeline to the large rectangular device in the kitchen, the fridge, and checked its contents.

“It’s full, it’s full!”

That black box was around as tall as a grown man, and the chilly inside was filled with various vegetables, fruits, and rows of bottles. Since Alma was the only one who used this place, there was not too much fresh produce, while the bottles took up more than half the space in the fridge.

“Wait, could these be…could it be…!”

The bottles gave a clear view of the colorful liquids filling them, some being red, others purple, or ambar, and so on. Mira’s interest was piqued, and a certain possibility flashed in her mind. Driven by it, she quickly opened one of the bottles, letting a rich aroma fill her nostrils.

“Ohh…how fragrant…”

The bottles were filled with liquor. The assortment included various types of wine from different fruits, beer, whiskey, and even sake. There was anything one could desire.

Mira had known that Alma was fond of drinking even back in the game days, and seeing all of those bottles, it was clear that that had not changed. And now Mira was starting to get curious about it too.

She had drank with Solomon before, which had left a strong impression on her, as expected from a king’s cellar.

With that precedent, she had high hopes of the drinks in front of her now. Alma was particularly fond of drinking, and this was her private selection for her own enjoyment. Not to mention that Nirvana was a far larger and more powerful country than Arkite.

It was impossible not to be tempted to try those drinks, enjoyed by one of the most influential people.

“If it’s just one shot…”

She reached out to one of the bottles, and then stopped before closing the fridge.

Despite her curiosity, she was going to meet the oracle soon after, a person she had to watch over personally. Being drunk would not be a good first impression.

+++

# **329: The Empress’ Selection – Summer**

The temptation of Alma’s collection of liquor had failed, but Mira was still curious about other things there.

Determined to comb through and see everything, she opened the freezer next.

“Oh, is that…”

A frosty breeze was released from the freezer and Mira noticed that half of it was filled with crystal clear ice, almost invisible, and was most certainly used by Alma to chill down her drinks. The other half of the freezer was filled with various wooden boxes packed neatly.

Wondering what could be in them, Mira took one and opened it before letting out a cry of joy. A waft of vanilla rose from the box once the lid was removed.

The content of that wooden box was ice cream.

Mira was convinced that the ice cream picked by the empress of a large empire had to be a delicacy in its own right, so she quickly nabbed one of the boxes, looked for a spoon in the kitchen, and sat back on the sofa to try a spoonful.

“…! This richness, sweetness, and strong milkiness! This is no mere lacto ice, it’s ice milk!”

Mira attempted to appraise the flavor, which only revealed her cheap knowledge, as she licked clean the box of ice cream. Then she instantly stood up and ran over to the freezer to fetch another box.

“Wait…this one is yogurt flavored! …Does that mean there’s other flavors too?!”

The first spoonful from the second box had a fresh tartness and sweetness to it. The boxes themselves had looked the same on the outside, except for the small tag on the lid that read Yogurt. The freezer was filled with more than just vanilla ice cream.

Mira had no doubt that all of the other flavors were just as wonderful, and began to search for a chair to set up camp right in front of the freezer for easier access.

And then she caught sight of an even better option.

There was a small yet elegant balcony, past a large sliding window that at first she thought only gave a view of the blue sky, which would offer the best vantage point.

“Ohh, that feels so luxurious just looking at it!”

She could only imagine what it would feel like to sit there, the empress’ personal balcony in the palace, which was already on a higher altitude than the rest of the city. That view would surely make the ice cream taste even better.

Unable to contain herself, she ran over to the window, slid it over, and went out to the balcony.

Above, she could see a sunshade followed by an endless blue sky, and as she lowered her gaze, the cityscape finally came into view.

Breathtaking was the only possible way to describe the view of Ratnatraya from the palace. The buildings nearby were all elegant and decently tall, their walls painted with soft colors.

But there was almost a gradient as the distance grew and the city changed, with colors becoming more vibrant, and the buildings appearing more rustic but still newly built.

“Now this is what an empress should see.”

The view from Arkite’s castle had also been impressive, but it did not compare to the scale of Ratnatraya. At the same time, it was a reminder of the higher responsibility Alma’s shoulders carried.

As the empress, Alma likely saw that city as a reflection of herself… But Mira had no such thoughts, as she just shouted, “This will be my special seat!” and happily sat there and enjoyed the view in bliss.

“Ah, there’s the venue for the whole tournament. I can see it so well from here…”

After yogurt, chocolate, banana, and more flavors of ice cream, Mira got bored of merely eating and started paying more attention to the scenery.

Straight ahead, there was the large stadium for the tournament, which appeared like a colorful and vivid spot amidst the city. The various attractions that were being set up around it were also visible from afar, making it look more and more like an amusement park.

“Ohh, I hadn’t noticed those food stalls before. I’ll have to go eat there next!”

Mira closely examined the surroundings, getting a clear view despite being so many kilometers away. She was doing that with the Skill Distant View, coupled with her newly learned Concept Art Telescope, giving her around fifty times magnification, making it seem like she was right there on the streets.

She used that to search for food stalls that seemed appealing to her, while not forgetting to keep eating ice cream. The only downside was that Telescope required her to form a ring with her fingers to create a magnifying lens within, so she had to stop looking whenever she wanted to eat.

“Oh, I think that’s where they were hiding.”

As she continued eating the ice cream, she kept looking around the city, muttering that as she spotted a large mansion. That was where the assassins had been hiding, and where Mira captured Jorg.

“Ohoh, they’ve cordoned off the whole area already.”

Curious to see how that place was doing, she used Distant View and Telescope to examine the area, seeing that the building had been closed off by the guards. That barrier would likely remain in place until they were done searching through the entire mansion, as it had been used as a hideout by Ira Muerte and likely could provide various leads.

(Hm, and there she is…Cecilia I think. Hmhm, I see, so she’s still in charge of the search there.)

As she continued watching, she spotted a certain woman through one of the windows. Cecilia was a knight with a strong defense, in various senses. She was leading the search there, and seemed to be quite excited to do it.

“Sorry for taking so long, I’m finally done… Wait, I gave you permission to eat, but you’re clearly overdoing it now, you’ll upset your stomach, grandpa.”

Alma finished her duties half an hour after Mira started eating ice cream, and five minutes after Mira left the balcony and went back inside. It had taken Alma a bit longer than planned to free herself, and the first thing she saw when she entered the room were seven empty boxes on the table, and Mira lying blissfully on the sofa.

“Nah, I’m fine. It takes a lot more than this to take down my stomach!”

Mira quickly raised her body and announced that with a lively voice, then adding, “They were all delicious,” with a chuckle.

“Unbelievable…”

Alma was half baffled and half resigned as she just shook her head, walking over to sit in front of Mira and changing topics, “So about your bodyguard mission…”

In response, Mira quickly sat up straight to listen more carefully. They were no longer talking about ice cream, but one of the biggest secrets of the empire.

They began by recapping their talks from the previous day, and then moved on to discuss the expected effects from that mission.

“I doubt they’ll act right away once they find out we’ve switched bodyguards, and instead try to watch from a distance to gain more information. Hopefully.”

Once Mira became the oracle’s bodyguard, the enemy would likely spend a few days trying to get a grasp of the situation.

Noin, the current bodyguard, could no longer get close to the oracle, so he was being swapped out for Mira, a strong adventurer who had recently risen in fame, who could approach the oracle without issues. There was a chance the enemy would think of it as the perfect chance and rush in to attack right away, but more than likely they would spend some time gauging Mira’s strength and trying to learn more about her…

“Hmm, I see.”

Mira still needed to be ready in the off-chance they attacked right away, and nodded as the thought of countermeasures.

They continued talking about things, and eventually began discussing more personal things about the oracle.

She was a fourteen year old girl called Iris, and was quite the spirited girl despite being branded with a serious title like oracle.

“Tonight is her scheduled time to use her power, so we’ll tell her about you being her new bodyguard at that time too.”

“Sounds good.”

Iris’ special power allowed her to read what someone else did and was thinking of doing, just by touching an item deeply linked to the target, like a strand of hair.

Its biggest strength was that there was no time limit to it, allowing her to continue reading a target for as long as the item was available, providing updated information.

Thanks to that power, one of the main leaders of Ira Muerte, He Who Commands the Dark Routes, August Gradin, had been largely hamstrung on the things he could do.

The only downside was that the longer that power was used, the more the target would also start to obtain information back from the oracle.

That was how August found out about the oracle and sent out assassins after her. On top of that, he used rather nasty means to terrorize the oracle, leading to her developing a phobia towards men and becoming afraid of Noin, one of the Twelve Apostles and her bodyguard, who could no longer fulfill his duty properly.

That was when Mira arrived, who was just as effective as Noin, and relieved him of his duty. That was a summary of the events leading to the present time.

Mira’s job was to be the oracle’s new bodyguard for the duration of the tournament. If everything went well, then Alma’s Twelve Apostles and secret service would finish sniffing out the remaining members of Ira Muerte and catching them.

It would obviously be a complex operation, but that was the gist of it.

“By the way, what happened with the assassins I caught before? Were you able to get any useful information out of them?”

Once they were done talking about the oracle, Mira suddenly brought that up.

Mira had randomly ran into a group of assassins who were already trying to get to the oracle, and ended up discovering and taking over their entire hideout. Their leader had been a man called Jorg, who seemed to be deeply knowledgeable about their organization.

“Mm, about that…he’s really good at keeping his mouth shut, so it’s not really going the best.”

Alma let out a sigh as she replied. They had tried questioning him a lot, but he would not let out a single word. He even turned out to be resistant to various truth serums.

“He was probably trained just for such situations. Even our strongest drug only made him grin at us, so it’s going to take some time before we can get something out of him.”

Alma added that they were currently using a different drug to lower his immunity to truth serums, which eventually should make them work on him and get him to confess.

The only issue was that the drug could be dangerous when administered too quickly, and it would take around two months before Jorg would speak.

“Two months seems like a lot of time.”

“Ideally, I’d like to get more information before the tournament starts in earnest…since all of our collaborators will arrive by then, but we’re stumped here.”

Jorg potentially had access to information relating to the spies currently infiltrating Nirvana, their identity, and what role they had taken. Maybe even information on which part of the tournament staff was being targeted the most.

There was also a chance he had been in contact with the higher-ups of Ira Muerte and could offer more insight on who they were, making his knowledge very valuable.

Sadly, it would take a long time before they were successful with the interrogation. In her frustration, Alma even joked about using banned drugs to force him to confess, which seemed to help her calm down and think more reasonably again.

+++

# **330: Professional**

“But wait, does this mean you haven’t developed any spells for such situations? I’m sure you have the resources for that, considering the size of your country.”

Using drugs would take two months, but maybe relying on spells could provide faster results.

Mira brought that possibility up, her voice having a tinge of jealousy for Nirvana’s available budget for research. There were many experiments the Silver Linked Towers had to give up on, which could have been made possible with the resources of a larger country.

“We are trying, yes. But I can’t help but think you’re just being sarcastic… I mean, I haven’t heard anything about something like that being developed in those towers of yours, so what makes you think we’ve been successful?”

As usual, the Silver Linked Towers were always at the forefront of spellcaster research. Nirvana’s own research centers usually took the results from the Towers and expanded upon them, in exchange for a considerable sum.

“Or rather, shouldn’t you tell me? Did they find a way to do that? Are they running any experiments already? You should know, right? I don’t care if it’s still a prototype, just tell me, please.”

Alma’s current situation was so irritating that she began pressing Mira for an answer.

“Hmmm… Yes, they’re trying to develop something like that in the Towers, but it’s hardly useful at the moment. It pretty much only gets the target extremely inebriated, so they can’t really string words together in a coherent manner and it’s very difficult to get usable information.”

Mira had visited all the Towers during her break after finding Lastrada and Artesia, so she had a good idea of what they were working on.

This was an experiment she had seen in the Tower of Concepts.

The current results were just as she had mentioned, random gibberish that could hardly be considered a confession. On top of that, it put the targets in such an intoxicated state that sometimes they would fully hallucinate whatever they said.

“I see… Hmm… But maybe he’ll still slip up and say something… Even a little…”

The information locked in Jorg’s head was extremely valuable, but there were no means of getting it out, which was pushing Alma to her wits’ end as she began mumbling.

Maybe even the incomplete confession spell could randomly get something useful out of him.

“No, you probably should give up on that one. I’ve seen one of the experiments, and the responses were completely nonsensical.”

Mira spoke with a firm voice, stating just how rough that spell still was, and Alma just lowered her head in dejection.

“Actually, there’s another spell that works much better, so I’d suggest giving that one a try.”

Mira grinned as she said that right after Alma seemed to give up, mentioning that she knew of a spell that was more effective than the prototype from the Tower of Concepts.

“…Huh? There is one?!”

The moment she heard that, Alma’s clouded eyes lit up as she rushed up to Mira, leaning over her while saying, “What spell is it?! Tell me! I’ll let you eat all the ice cream you want!” determined to learn more.

“Calm down, I’ll tell you, don’t worry.”

Mira tried to get Alma to calm down first, as she kept insisting, “hurry, hurry!” before explaining the situation.

“The other spell I know of happens to be an Onmyoji Art…”

There had been one person who had accomplished the same result the Tower of Concepts was trying to achieve with their spell.

The results were guaranteed, as Mira had witnessed it herself, and it would surely be of use to obtain information from Jorg as well.

“There’s only one little issue. It’s a really complex and difficult spell, which compounds with how much the target resists. Currently, only the creator of that spell can use it properly.”

A spell like that could be extremely useful if it could be learned easily, but using it involved very specific conditions.

Put simply, the spell put the target into a fully hypnotized state, which required a complex ritual, coupled with possessing enough strength to break through any resistance the target showed.

“So I just have to get the creator to come here, right? Where is that person… Wait, huh? Did you just say it’s an Onmyoji Art? Does that mean…”

It was a really difficult spell, and Mira made it seem like only a master of Onmyoji Arts would be able to use it, which led to a certain possibility.

If it was too difficult, there was only one person that came into Alma’s mind.

“…Kagura?! Tell me, did you find Kagura already?!”

The only realistic option was Kagura, which would mean that Mira had already successfully tracked down another of the missing Wisemen, and judging by Alma’s elated reaction, she had also been good friends with Kagura.

“Yes, I did not too long ago. It wasn’t even that hard.”

Mira gloated about her achievement seeing how excited Alma got, smugly mentioning that Artesia was not the only one she had found so far.

“So you know where she is! That’s so good to hear, so Kagura is around too.”

Mira had not only found Alma’s sister-in-law that had been missing for more than thirty years, but another of her good friends too. Then she quickly moved on to planning, “So you’re still waiting for the right moment to make the public announcement? Should I try to find a way to get her here in secret?”

Seeing her friend again was reason enough, but Kagura was also the only person who could use the spell Alma needed, so she wanted to bring Kagura to Nirvana as soon as possible.

Sadly, things would not be so simple. Alma was under the impression that Kagura was back in Arkite, but that was not quite right.

“Ah…actually, there’s a bit of a problem with that. Kagura still had some work to do, so she hasn’t returned yet. And I actually have no idea where she is at the moment…”

Currently, Kagura was traveling together with the Angel Tiriel, visiting the various Demon Coffins…places like the one that gave rise to Chimera Clauzen, to ensure they were all sealed properly.

That was a mission they had to keep secret, so not even Mira knew where they were, and it was hard to say whether Kagura would be free to come over to Nirvana.

“Huh? Really?! I mean, I guess it makes sense for her to be busy too, but still…”

Alma glared at Mira, as if telling her to stop giving her false hope like that. Meanwhile, Mira recoiled and looked away awkwardly, as she had only been trying to show off the fact she knew such a spell.

At the same time, Mira was not the kind of person to apologize and give up.

“No…that’s not it… I mean, she might not be back home, but there’s a way to contact her. You know her, I’m sure she’ll be more than willing to help once she hears our situation!”

They needed Kagura’s help to obtain information necessary to destroy the evil organization Ira Muerte.

Kagura had already been fighting a similar organization in the past when taking down Chimera Clauzen, so she would fully understand Alma’s situation.

On top of that, Kagura also had the unique ability of switching places with one of her shikigami. So there was little stopping her from flying over as soon as she was contacted.

Mira spoke with conviction, fully aware of all that, but Alma looked at her half hopeful and half doubtful.

“So, how do we contact her then?!”

Alma delved straight to the biggest hurdle with that idea, and Mira averted her gaze again. After all, it was impossible to contact Kagura without knowing where she was.

“Ummm, I mean, about that…”

Mira desperately tried to think of a solution, her eyes swimming around nervously as she thought, eventually catching a glimpse of the blue sky.

She was already starting to have strange delusions, thinking that maybe Piisuke would randomly fly in, and then she had an actual idea.

Even if she could not contact Kagura directly, she still had associates. The Fifty Bells’ headquarters, to be more specific. Alioth had been put in charge of the Fifty Bells after they got rid of Chimera Clauzen’s remnants, but Kagura was still their leader. They had to still be in contact, even while Kagura went to check on the coffins.

So if Mira and Alma got in contact with the headquarters, they would pass on the message to Kagura.

And knowing Kagura, as soon as she received the message, she would send Piisuke to visit. The rest was easy. Kagura would switch places with Piisuke, use her interrogation spell, and all of Jorg’s secrets would be revealed.

Contacting the headquarters was also easy. After all, Mira had the number to call, and she had a device to make the call in her wagon.

“Heheh, just listen closely!”

Mira haughtily raised her voice and reached into her pocket…wanting to bring out the note with the Fifty Bells’ headquarters number…

“…Hm?”

But it was missing, her Item Box did not have it either, and even as she emptied her bag with all her research notes, she was unable to find it.

“What’s wrong, Grandpa? Hurry up already!”

“It’s just…”

Alma was still full of hope, while Mira’s cockiness turned to desperation.

She checked every single pocket she had, and as a last recourse, attempted to recall the numbers, but with her memory, that was like trying to make out a distant sign on a foggy day.

“…Ah!” and then Mira realized her own folly.

The last time she had seen that piece of paper was back when she found Lastrada and Artesia, as they wanted to borrow the spirit flying ship to carry the hundred children in their orphanage.

As far as she remembered, she placed that note in a pocket of her clothes after that. And the outfit she was wearing at the time was her custom Magic Robe Set for summer.

She was currently wearing the autumn set. In other words, she had left the note in her previous clothes back home.

(…Oh right, I think Mariana mentioned something about putting everything from my pockets on my desk…)

Mira had put those clothes aside to be washed, and she faintly remembered what happened around that time, putting her in more distress. She pressed her lips together, desperately trying to think of an excuse…or rather a solution.

“It couldn’t be that you’ve forgotten yet another thing, could it?”

Alma was starting to get suspicious, especially after Mira put on airs so much.

“N-No, that’s definitely not it.”

Mira laughed awkwardly, trying to play things off, internally pivoting to her wagon and if she could find a solution there.

She had no choice but to abide her shame and call the Tower of Summoning and tell Mariana or Creos to find the note for her.

And then she realized that after a month of constant research and experiments, she had no idea where on her desk that note could be. It was so cluttered with random books and pieces of paper that she could not even begin to describe where it was.

(Hmmm…how do I contact the headquarters… Hm? If they’re headquarters…!)

Every time she thought of a solution, she ran into another wall, until she eventually returned to more realistic ideas. There was another way of getting in contact with the Fifty Bells’ headquarters.

“Umm…_Ahem_, just out of curiosity, have you heard of an organization called the Fifty Bells?”

Mira decided to ask that, really not wanting to admit that she had just been putting on airs.

The Fifty Bells was the organization Kagura had established to take down Chimera Clauzen. But that was kept secret, and openly they declared to be an environmentalist organization that wanted to preserve forests for spirits to live in.

“Yup, I’ve heard of them. They’re the guys taking care of forests and stuff, right? I heard they’ve been campaigning a lot more recently, something about expanding the eastern forest by 2% or something like that.”

Alma barely had to think about it, instantly knowing who they were. They were active across the whole continent, so almost everyone had heard their name.

And since they had accomplished their main goal of taking down Chimera Clauzen, they had a lot more time for their outward presence, explaining their recent rise in activity. All the people and resources once used to fight were being used for the forests’ sake.

They also seemed to be active in Nirvana, judging from Alma’s reaction. That made it easier to narrow down what Mira wanted to know.

“Then I’m guessing they also have a branch in this country, do you know in which city it is?”

That was the solution Mira had thought of. Finding the closest branch of the Fifty Bells.

Kagura had mentioned they had such branches in various countries, and all of them had the means to communicate with the headquarters.

If she could not use her wagon to call the headquarters, she could just do it through a branch.

She had almost lost it when she realized the note was gone, but a branch would be her salvation. And she happened to be in a big and influential country. There had to be a branch there, so she put all her hope on that and waited for Alma’s answer.

+++

# **331: Warm Reception**

With the note missing, Mira had no way of contacting the Fifty Bells’ headquarters from her wagon. But she still had a chance if they had a branch in Nirvana. Mira waited with anticipation, while Alma took a moment to think about it.

“A branch hmm… I think it’s somewhere near the east gate. They mentioned they wanted to be as close to the forest as possible, and they found a vacant building there for quite cheap.”

That had happened around a decade in the past, so Alma was not too sure about all the details. She just remembered that it was somewhere near the east gate. Still, that was enough for Mira to go off on.

“Oh! The east gate? So the branch is in this city? You really are the best!”

The Fifty Bells had branches all over the continent, but Kagura had mentioned that often it was located in remote locations, depending on the country.

Here in Nirvana, Alma had allowed the branch to be instated in the capital city, which was pretty much the best outcome they could have wanted.

That had been quite kind of the empress, and it also meant Mira did not have to travel to another city, so she happily praised Alma for that decision.

“Huh? Was that a compliment? Wait, no, what does the Fifty Bells’ branch have anything to do with this? I thought we were talking about Kagura… Hold on a moment—”

Alma blushed for a moment, as it was rare for her to get compliments, only to be confused by the sudden change in topic, and then stopped suddenly as she remembered something. After a short pause, she said, “By the way, it’s nothing official yet, just a rumor one of my informants caught wind of…”

The rumor she had heard was something Nirvana’s secret service had discovered independently, revolving around a certain person involved in the fight against Chimera Clauzen.

“Most people just talk about the famous adventurers and guilds there, like Jack Grave or Eleonora, and you too Grandpa. But I heard that there was also someone less known who goes by the name of Alioth.”

So far, that was largely a preamble, before Alma went straight to the main point.

As it turned out, the person who came to request permission to instate the Fifty Bells’ branch looked identical to this Alioth. And that was not all. Alma’s secret service had looked into Alioth some more, and discovered that he was acting under orders of someone called Uzume.

“The Fifty Bells’ mission is to preserve the forests where spirits live, right? So that would make Chimera Clauzen their main enemy.”

Alma mentioned that, explaining why it made sense for them to be involved in that fight.

“I always assumed that Uzume was just the highest commander of the Fifty Bells, but you were there, grandpa. Do you know more? I mean, I even heard that Uzume is supposed to be a really strong Onmyoji Master, and you’re suddenly asking about their branch. It all connects, doesn’t it?”

Everything was slowly connecting as Alma brought up the information she knew, and when everything was put together, she discovered the truth. The leader of the Fifty Bells was Kagura.

“Hm, I expected no less from your information network. You know a lot already.”

Mira asking for the location of the branch was all Alma needed to figure everything out. Impressed by it, Mira confirmed that Kagura was the leader of the Fifty Bells, and gave a brief explanation of how that came to be.

She also mentioned how Kagura was traveling with the Angel Tiriel now that Chimera Clauzen had been defeated. Also how Kagura was the one who had developed that interrogation spell, and that the branches had a way of communicating with the headquarters.

“…So if we pass a message through the branch, I’m sure it’ll get to Kagura eventually. And unless she’s in a lot of trouble, she should come here as soon as possible, and it should still be faster than waiting two months for your drugs to work.”

Knowing Kagura, as long as she was not completely swamped with work, she would offer her help. The only setback would depend on how often Kagura got in touch with the headquarters, but Mira was sure that it had to be more frequent than once every few months.

Chimera Clauzen had been an enormous organization, so even after their defeat, there were many people connected to them that still needed to see justice. That meant the Fifty Bells still had multiple ongoing operations, which would require Kagura’s opinion and orders to be conducted.

“I see, so that’s why you wanted to know about the branch. And if they send the message, then Kagura will come here… Okay yes, I have hope again!”

Now that she understood everything, Alma hopped on her feet and said, “Let’s go ask them then!” even adding that she was the one asking for the favor, so it was only right for her to go as well.

But Mira noticed what was happening. She had seen that behavior before in Solomon.

“No, it’s enough for me to go alone. I mean, it won’t do for the empress to be wandering around the city like that, and you have plenty of work yourself, so just wait for me.”

For some reason, rulers seemed to have the habit of trying to find any excuse possible to run away from their duties. Mira instantly noticed it was happening again, so she put an end to it and stood up as well.

Soon, Mira was going to be appointed the oracle’s new bodyguard, so it was better to leave the message now.

“Ack…!”

Seeing Alma’s reaction only proved Mira’s hunch right. She stammered for a moment, but did not give up on her escape just yet. She fell silent for a moment, thinking of another reason to go with Mira, looking determined to do it.

“Also, not just everyone can get access to the branch’s communication device. You need to know a specific password before they let you into that room. It doesn’t matter that you’re the empress, or rather, it’s because you’re the empress that you shouldn’t just try to force your way in there.”

Mira spoke with a stern and admonishing voice.

Obviously enough, the room to communicate with the headquarters was off-limits from the general public. Only members of the Fifty Bells were allowed in there.

Being the empress, Alma could probably use her authority to force her way there, but Mira did not think that would be a respectable use of power.

And to cap it off, Mira proudly announced, “But I do know the password.”

Mira had placed such a call in the past, and the Fifty Bells’ Hidden Sasori had told her the password. So she insisted that it was best for her to go alone.

“Ah, but wait, you don’t know where the branch is, right? So I’ll show you the way.”

Alma’s eyes lit up as she thought of that, but Mira saw straight through her lies.

“What do you mean? Just earlier you said you don’t remember the exact location.”

Earlier, when Mira first mentioned the branch, Alma said that it was somewhere near the east gate, but could not remember the exact details. So in short, Alma could not guide Mira there.

“…Okay okayyy, I’ll keep being tortured by deskwork and wait for you.”

In the end, her own words had destroyed her chances of leaving, and Alma capitulated. She turned around and waddled back to her office, pouting and sulking the entire time.

But she had not given up entirely yet, as she languidly reached for the pile of paper and let out a very evident sigh, her eyes locked on Mira the entire time.

“It looks like you have it rough. I guess leading a large country also comes with a lot of work.”

There were obviously various other ministers and officers who took care of other duties, but there were always things that required the empress’ direct approval.

When Mira seemed to recognize the immense amount of work, Alma looked up with hope, as she really wanted to get away from it all even if it was just for a short moment.

After all, interrogating Jorg was an important matter, and Alma could use that as a valid reason to leave the palace. But that would require Mira’s approval too, since it was Mira who was familiar with the Fifty Bells.

“I’ll take my time getting there, and when coming back, so just hang in there.”

And because of that, Mira mercilessly trampled on that hope. Alma shouted, “Grandpa you bullyyy!” as Mira headed out to search for the Fifty Bells’ branch near the east gate.

After leaving the palace, Mira summoned Pegasus and flew east, watching the city below her for around five minutes before she landed in front of a large gate.

The city walls were at least fifty meters tall, and the gate built into it was around twenty meters tall. But it remained closed, and it had hardly ever been opened.

That was no surprise, since the only thing to the east of the city was a vast forest, and there were no other cities or towns in that direction.

The only people who went in that direction were adventurers and hunters who made a living off the wilderness, and they did not need to pass through the large gate, as there was a smaller door for people next to it.

In recent years, the large gate had only been opened when the army conducted training exercises in the forest.

Because of all those factors, this section of the city was the least noisy one, compared to the other three gates.

“It really is so tall…”

After sending Pegasus away, Mira looked up at the gate and the walls that stretched far above it.

Despite it being the least used gate, the walls there were still much taller compared to the other gates.

It had been built that way by design, since the forest on the other side had many tall trees, and some monsters could climb on them and then attempt to jump over the wall.

(That reminds me, there was a time I helped defend the city from them.)

As she thought back to a time when a high level beast had spawned in the forest, and she fought alongside the Twelve Apostles, Mira walked over to the guard station next to the gate. The gatekeeper there would surely know a lot about the buildings around there.

That was the most efficient way to find the Fifty Bells’ branch, asking someone who was familiar with that area.

There was an armed soldier standing in front of the station, and nearby there was also a bulletin board with various wanted posters.

The posters mainly depicted murderers, as those tended to be the worst criminals who deserved being hunted down like that. But there were others as well, even including a beautiful woman.

She was branded as a thief, who would first drain men of their energy, and then make off with all their belongings.

(Somehow…I doubt they regretted that end.)

Harboring those thoughts while looking at the bulletin board, Mira approached the gatekeeper.

“Hello there, can I ask something real quick?”

When Mira spoke to him, he turned around with a smile and replied, “Hm? What is it, did you get lost?”

She really wanted to shout, “I’m not a child!” but contained herself, silently shaking her head.

“No, I’m not lost. I’m just trying to get somewhere. I was told the Fifty Bells have a branch around here, would you happen to know where it is?”

By now she was used to being mistaken for a lost child. Or rather, she had accepted the fact that it would happen commonly, and got better at moving things along quickly instead of having to explain things for long.

“I see, so you’re just running errands. It’s not really far from here, go around that corner there and find the general store. You’ll see a big building behind it. That’s where you want to go.”

The gatekeeper replied while pointing to a corner nearby and carefully gave Mira directions. In the end, he was still treating Mira as a child, not a lost one, but one running errands, and there was little Mira could do about that.

“I appreciate your assistance.”

Mira tried her best to act like an older person as she thanked him, and then headed to that store he mentioned, and along the way…

(Wait? Why did he mention errands?)

Somehow, the gatekeeper’s first reaction to hearing about the Fifty Bells’ branch was to assume it was for errands, and Mira could not understand why.

When she had visited the branch in Sentopolly, she had seen a small inconspicuous house, where the branch director Mattie was researching how to grow plants in the wastelands. Mira could not see a reason why anyone would regularly visit such a place.

In the end, Mira decided it was not worth the effort to think too hard about it, so she turned around the corner and continued walking.

+++

# **332: The Fifty Bells, Ratnatraya Branch**

As she followed the gatekeeper’s directions, she turned onto a small street around the corner. It was barely wide enough for two carriages to pass side by side, and even then the coaches would have to maneuver with great care.

At least, that was the theory. In reality, it would probably be impossible for carriages to do so at all, with signboards jutting out everywhere and pedestrians occupying much of the street.

Mira soon noticed that it was a lively street too, with various shops lined up one after another. There were bakeries offering freshly baked bread, relaxing cafes, shops selling odd Magic Wares, and a bleak weapons store. There was a bit of everything there.

“Behind the general store…I think this is it? But it doesn’t look right.”

After walking down the street and looking at the various shops, she faced a certain building with a puzzled look. It was the place the gatekeeper had mentioned, but it did not look like a branch of the Fifty Bells.

“Large variety of herbs and high quality medicinal plants…hmm.”

Mira read the sign placed in front of that building, then looked through one of the windows, seeing a front counter and a lot of pots with plants.

The building she had been guided to turned out to be another shop.

(Did I mess up somewhere along the way?)

She could not imagine that this was the Fifty Bells’ branch, so she went back the way she came and looked at the other buildings nearby more closely.

In the end, she could not find any other building that looked like the correct one, so Mira returned to the first one she found.

For a moment, she began wondering if they had moved somewhere else, and then she recalled what the gatekeeper had said. Errands.

“No, it couldn’t be…”

The most common errand for children to run was shopping. Coupling that with the store she found, it all made sense in a way. With that in mind, Mira looked at the store again.

The first thing she noticed was a sign that read, “Recommendation of the day,” listing the names of various herbs, including some rather rare ones.

“Oh, they have Tocopecco leaves in stock.”

That was a herb she had heard about from an adventurer in the Ancient Underground City, who was good at cooking and mentioned those leaves paired well with meat. The sign claimed they had a large amount of freshly picked high quality leaves.

She continued looking around, remembering the taste from back then, and noticed another sign, larger than the recommended one.

“Hmm… Everforest Garden, huh.”

It was not particularly hidden, but also did not stand out a lot, being placed right on top of the entrance. That was probably the name of the store, and Mira noticed smaller letters just below.

They were written in a pleasant green, and were easy to miss, but they definitely read Fifty Bells Ratnatraya Branch.

“So this actually was the branch all along…”

Mira had failed to consider the possibility that the branches could be different from the one in Sentopolly. In reality, they varied a lot depending on the country.

Then again, Sentopolly was under the control of Chimera Clauzen at the time, who were enemies with the Fifty Bells, so it made sense that the branch was not very big. But they were not chased out of there either, since in the public eye the Fifty Bells were a charity organization dedicated to protecting forests, and it would cast a bad light on Sentopolly if they openly pushed them away. So in the end, the branch was allowed to exist as a small house in the industrial district.

“Ohh…it’s so different here.”

Mira stepped into the branch, and looked around the first floor, which was no different from a store.
