Iris’ life was confined to her room, and despite all of Alma’s efforts to make it enjoyable, it was clear she yearned to see more of the outside world.

Mira quickly caught up on that, so she happily helped Iris satiate her curiosity.

The only exception was when the conversation turned to the latest love stories around the city.

Alma and Iris seemed really into the conversation, while Mira could not follow at all so she just remained silent, doing her best to ignore Martel’s excited voice constantly echoing in her head.

+++

# **338: The Possibilities of Magic Engineering**

“You’ve traveled in one before?! That’s so cool!”

“Yes, they were huge machines.”

Alma and Iris’ conversation took various turns before circling back to the continental railroads, which allowed Mira to join back in, leading to a lengthy conversation between the two.

That had been the objective of the sushi party all along, allowing those two to establish a friendship as quickly as possible, and it had been quite successful.

This was the first time they had met, and Iris was already very friendly with Mira, as well as seeing her in an admiring way.

And the longer they spoke, the more time they had for their stomachs to settle down.

By the time they could move again, the three began to clean up after lunch, until Alma intervened and said she would take care of it, and that the other two should just sit back and rest.

It seemed like Alma really wanted to let Mira tell Iris many stories about the world outside.

“Well, if that’s what you want.”

Mira replied to Alma, and went to indulge Iris’ curiosity, essentially chronicling all her travels around the continent.

It was not limited to her adventures in dungeons like the Ancient Temple or the Primal Forest either, also mentioning the various cities she visited, the different sceneries she saw, and so on, which Iris listened to with much attention.

Eventually, they were interrupted by a sound like a harp being strummed.

“Hm? What was that noise just now?”

Only Mira, Alma, and Iris were there, and none of them had made that sound.

That made Mira wonder just what that had been, and Iris quickly gave her an answer, “That’s the signal that one of the Twelve Apostles is here!”

As it turned out, there was a sound notification system linked to the doors leading into the room, which would produce a different noise depending on which key was used.

The Twelve Apostles would produce a harp sound, while Alma’s resembled a piano.

“Hmm, I see. So there’s a system like that in place too. I wasn’t informed.”

Mira nodded in approval, while also glaring at Alma. That was the kind of information she really wanted to have beforehand, especially as she had to work as Iris’ bodyguard.

But Alma seemed rather flustered, and not because of Mira’s resentful stare.

“Oh no…she’s actually coming here directly…”

She muttered to herself as she headed to the sink and began washing the dishes with extreme care.

Mira could only wonder what was happening, and it did not take long before it all became clear.

“Good afternoon, Iris. And you too Mira, thank you again for agreeing to be the new bodyguard.”

The visitor turned out to be Esmeralda, who politely greeted everyone there. She was there looking for Alma, who had been missing for a long time by now.

“I had a hunch I’d find you here.”

Esmeralda said with a sigh, seeing Alma in the kitchen washing dishes.

“There’s still a lot of work left to do.” She added that while she walked toward Alma. Her voice was calm, but it conveyed a lot of pressure.

“I would go, but look at all these dishes I still need to wash.”

All Alma could do was try to come up with such excuses.

As it turned out, the main reason why Alma had decided to do all the cleaning herself was so she could stay there for as long as possible, neglecting her office duties.

“In that case let me help you get it done faster.”

Esmeralda was already used to Alma’s excuses, so still looking perfectly calm, she entered the kitchen and began washing the dishes at a terrifying speed.

Meanwhile, Alma tried to sabotage those efforts however she could. But in the end, it only took around three minutes before Alma no longer had any reasons left to be there.

“Well then, I’ll leave the rest in your hands, Mira.”

Saying that, Esmeralda took hold of Alma before she could resist, and began dragging her away.

But before Mira forgot, she brought up the issue from earlier. “Before you go, could you tell me about all the defense systems installed here?”

“Wait, don’t tell me she didn’t brief you on anything yet?”

Esmeralda’s response was filled with a dangerous tone.

“Ummm, so a lot happened and umm…”

Alma just looked away nervously. After all, one would have expected that to be the first thing she told Mira about.

Then again, Iris had lost consciousness from being too hungry, and they had to rush getting lunch ready, which Alma claimed made her forget about it.

“Hmm… It’s also my fault for being delayed. Don’t blame her too much for it.”

To be precise, Mira had spent way too long talking about summoning on the phone, delaying her return. That was still eating at her consciousness, so she decided to shoulder some of the blame for Alma.

Having a third party’s opinion seemed to work, as Esmeralda said, “Alright, I understand,” and calmed down.

“I’m really sorry about all that, Mira. There’s a lot of people waiting for us so I can’t explain everything, but I’d swear we prepared a guidebook…”

Saying that, Esmeralda tugged lightly on Alma, urging her to do something.

“Ahhh, right, that guidebook. You should find everything you need in it, and Iris should be able to tell you a lot too.”

In response, Alma brought forth a small booklet that was branded as ‘ultra top secret,’ which detailed all of the defensive systems installed in the oracle’s room.

“Alright, got it.”

As soon as Mira took the booklet, Alma was dragged out of there by Esmeralda.

“Now then…”

With Alma going back to work, only Mira and Iris remained in the room.

That also meant that Mira was fully in charge of Iris’ safety now, so she decided to start by reading through the booklet…when she noticed that Iris was looking at her, like she was expecting something, or looking forward to something.

(What’s getting her so excited now…?)

Mira could not understand that reaction, and wondered about it until their gazes met. That seemed to be the signal Iris was waiting for.

“Let’s go then, Mira! I’ll show you around!”

Since Alma had mentioned that Iris also knew a lot, Iris had been looking forward to giving Mira a tour of the room and all its secrets. That was why she looked so excited.

Receiving a direct explanation from the person living here was also better than reading about it in a booklet.

“Okay, I’ll count on you.”

As soon as Mira replied, Iris beamed a smile and said, “I’ll do my best!” and ran out.

Then she realized she was rushing too much and she came back, her head peeking into the room, but she clearly did not regret it one bit.

“We’ll start from the first floor and go up in order, okay?!”

Her eyes were twinkling, urging Mira to follow her, ready to rush off any moment.

Only a handful of people were allowed in this room, as the oracle was an important person, who needed to be kept under maximum security. Only Alma and the female Apostles would visit her.

So now that there was a new face there, she was beside herself with joy. It was almost like this was her first time experiencing a sleepover.

And even then, the fact that she was this happy went to show just how few friends she really had.

“We’ve got plenty of time, no need to rush.”

Mira stashed the booklet away into her Item Box, and followed after Iris, ready to follow her wherever she wanted to go.

The main construction where Iris lived had a comparatively simple layout.

When seen from above, each floor was basically identical, like blocks stacked into a two by three grid. And the block on the top row and middle column were the stairs.

Iris wanted to show every floor in order, so they began with the first floor, which looked like a mix between a bar and a lobby. All of the blocks were joined together there, except for the stairs.

“There’s a lot of really tasty drinks here, so it’s the best place to relax after a bath.”

Iris then proceeded to bring up the ones she recommended, when she seemed to realize something and said, “Ah, I didn’t drink it yet today,” as she pulled out one bottle and poured herself a glass, drinking it all in one go.

“Bleghh…”

When she was done, she let out a groan rather unbecoming of a girl.

Mira asked what that drink was, and Iris replied that it was a herbal tea of a special blend of many medicinal plants. Alma had told her to drink a glass every day to stay healthy.

“This…is really intense…”

Mira decided to smell a bit of it, and scowled right after as her nose was assaulted by a grassy and overly herbal smell.

But oddly enough, it did smell like something healthy.[1](#easy-footnote-bottom-1-119620)　

Next, they went to the second floor, entering the room to the left of the stairs. That room was two blocks long, and it was the same living room Mira first entered when searching for Iris.

“Every time I sit on this chair I get sleepy really fast… And ah, these round things are called records, and when you put them on the machine it plays music.”

Iris was enjoying it so much that she went ahead and explained even the smallest things.

Eventually, she said, “And here’s my favorite one,” as she happily brought over the large chest on wheels that Mira had also seen before.

“Oh, now I’m looking forward to it too.”

Overall, it looked like a rather fancy box, but Iris said it was her favorite thing.

Considering just how much Alma, the empress, had spent furnishing the room, Mira already had very high expectations for whatever it was.

“Ta-daaa!”

Iris took hold of the handle on top and raised the cover, revealing a smaller box inside, which was around fifty centimeters tall, and around seventy wide and deep.

But it was clear that it was no mere box, as one of its sides was made of glass.

“Hmmm… This looks like some complicated device…”

Mira tried peering through the glass, but everything was dark inside, so it was not just a display case of some sort either.

Instead, she noticed various switches and buttons on the side, revealing that it was some sort of device made with Magic Engineering.

Seeing those switches, and the glass, Mira had a guess as to what the box was. But before she could say anything, Iris’ excitement won over as she began pressing the switches while saying, “You see, this is…”

The box activated after a short moment.

The instant Mira saw that, she raised her voice in shock, “I can’t believe it..!”

What she saw on the box’s glass was a scenery, completely different from what they had nearby. And it was not just that, there was also sound coming from the holes on the sides of the box.

In short, that box was a TV.

“This is called a Magic TV! It’s a really cool device that lets you see things from far away!”

Iris was smiling with delight as she switched around the picture, showing everything that was available.

There were various stage plays, the tournament’s pre-show, and various other broadcasts set up.

As Iris explained, there was a separate device called a Magic TV Scope, which would transmit whatever it saw to the Magic TV. And if they paired that with a Magic Mic, it would also transmit sounds.

The only limitation so far was that the sound and picture would arrive with different delays. But at least the picture was of a high resolution.

(I didn’t think they would’ve progressed this far already.)

Mira was impressed seeing the Magic TV in front of her.

It had only been a few months since Soul Howl had told her that someone from the Rising Sun Committee was working on TV equipment.

She did not know if this was the result of that, or if it had been developed independently by Nirvana. Either way, culture was progressing at a rapid pace.

“Now this is amazing.”

Mira nodded, approving of Iris’ choice of favorite item, and Iris replied with a bright smile.

“It really is!”

So far, Iris had met very few people, and they were all older and important people in the government, which meant they could not stay with her for long.

That was why she was beside herself with joy now that she had met Mira, who would be able to stay with her for longer and share in a lot of the things she found fun.

“You know, this place here…”

Since Mira had shown interest in the Magic TV, Iris’ motivation had been set aflame, so she quickly began explaining more things about it.

As it turned out, everything shown on the Magic TV was a live feed.

Currently there were Magic TV Scopes installed in the two large theaters of Ratnatraya, the two event stages of the public convention center, and two showing different angles of the tournament’s preliminary arena.

Things would get especially interesting once the tournament actually began, so Iris would make sure not to miss watching the TV the next day.

(I guess it’s not really her fault.)

Hearing that made Mira just a little bit worried, as it seemed like Iris could end up becoming addicted to the TV.

But there was not much that could be done about it, as she had to remain locked up for as long as that dangerous organization was after her.

For now, all Mira could do was think if there was anything else she could do other than being a bodyguard, so that Iris would be able to meet more people and have a more fulfilling life once she could go outside again.

#### **Footnotes:**

1. Syl: I mean… yea, a healthy smell is not a delicious smell

+++

# **339: Trap Room**

After agreeing on watching TV together later, the two left the living room and went across to the two blocks on the right side of the second floor.

Most of the water and plumbing were gathered there, so the toilet, laundry room, and bathroom were there.

“This is a pretty large area too…”

“It’s set up to be ready at any moment, so feel free to use it whenever you want to, Mira.”

The toilet and laundry room occupied half a block. The remaining block and a half were all for the bathroom. There was ample space to wash oneself, and a large bathtub. And it was not fully enclosed, giving a view to the lush garden outside.

(Taking a drink here would be the best.)

Just seeing that view made Mira look forward to taking a bath there.

Next, they went to the lower middle block, which faced the garden. That was the room where Iris performed her duties as oracle.

Iris was in charge of periodically spying on August, one of the higher-ups of Ira Muerte.

Thanks to that, they had been able to discover all the underground trading routes he used, ruining their business and costing them at least a couple hundred billion Rils. On top of that, August could no longer be involved in anything related to the organization, so he could not make up for their lost revenue either.

Ira Muerte had lost an awful amount of money, all thanks to Iris, and as long as she continued supervising August, he would never be able to do anything about it without it being found out.

That was why it was so important to keep Iris safe.

That night at nine o’clock, it would be Iris’ next turn to use her powers on August, to make sure he was not plotting anything.

With the second floor done, they went up to the third floor.

To the left was the same kitchen and dining area where they had had their sushi party earlier.

“You can make all sorts of food here!”

Iris showed her the kitchen, which Mira had not really looked at earlier.

There were all sorts of kitchen appliances there, as well as an oven, so Iris was right to say one could prepare anything there.

As it turned out, Iris was not just good at eating food, but also at making it, and was already planning to go all out making dinner that night.

After that, they passed through the middle block to cross over to the right side. That middle block was a balcony, once again providing a beautiful view of the garden.

The right side was the bedroom, painted in soft colors and adorned very cutely. There was also a huge pile of plush toys on the bed in the middle of the room, which would keep Iris at least some company at night.

“Mira, you can sleep here.”

There was a second bed in the room. It had a simpler shape, but it was no less impressive than Iris’.

“Oh…alright.”

Being her bodyguard also meant sleeping in the same room as her.

For a moment, Mira worried what Mariana would think if she found out that Mira was sleeping in the same room as another girl, but then shook those thoughts away as it was required for her job.

That concluded their tour of the third floor, and they went up to the fourth one.

“Now this is a sight to behold as well.”

Mira was once again shocked as she looked around the fourth floor.

As it turned out, the entire floor was filled with bookshelves.

There were so many it could be confused with a library, with books everywhere one turned. At first glance, it was clear there were easily at least ten thousand books there.

The walls were painted in plain white, and the wooden floor was polished nicely. The lights also had a warm tone, creating a pleasant and relaxing environment, distinct from the luxury that filled the previous floors.

Then again, sitting down to read in such a library would also be quite an experience.

“Alma had this built for me too, so I’m never bored. There’s all sorts of fun books here, so don’t feel afraid to check them out if you want!”

Saying that, Iris happily ran up to one of the bookshelves, adding, “Lately I’ve been getting into these books, they’re called comics. You should check them out!”

As it turned out, there were even comic books in that library.

Curious about them, Mira went to look at the bookshelf and noticed there were various titles she had not seen yet.

“There sure are a lot of them here.”

Mira was surprised to see an even larger variety than in most bookstores, and as she looked through them, she understood why.

There were various books that did not come from major publishers. Basically, they were what she once knew as doujin titles.

Solomon had once mentioned that during one of their chats, regarding how former players had brought various aspects of their culture, which permeated into this world for more than two decades.

Given that time, it made sense for people who were not former players to also become such artists. And as a result, there were plenty of minor independent releases.

All of that made Mira wonder how long it would take before that major convention also opened here…or maybe it already existed… And as she thought of all that, she noticed that one of the doujin series there was about the Nine Wisemen, which made her grimace a little.

(Shalwina would lose her mind if she saw this.)

There were also plenty of books other than comics in there, so it was like paradise for a bookworm like Shalwina.

As Mira thought of all that, Iris went up to other shelves, mentioning the books she had read and what she thought about them.

“Noin recommended this one to me. It’s a story about the search for five hidden treasures in the world, it was really exciting!”

Her explanations tended to be lackluster, but maybe she was just trying to avoid giving away too much about the stories.

At the same time, she was clearly excited to have a conversation partner, and it was evident she was having a great time as her face lit up constantly. Somehow, just watching her like that was enough for Mira to have fun as well, and they continued going around the various bookshelves.

Once they were done looking around the library, the tour came to an end and the two went to the living room to watch TV together.

There were all sorts of events being conducted every day in the tournament grounds, and now, a little past five in the afternoon, they were having a sort of music showdown.

It was a rather random event, with various performers, traveling bards, singers, bands, and anything else related to music. But that made it look like a festival, something anyone could enjoy watching.

Time seemed to blaze by like that, and before they realized, it was late at night. By then, Iris made sure to keep her promise and began preparing something in the kitchen.

She was going to make fried rice for dinner. Most ingredients like vegetables were already cut and ready to use, so she just needed to pick what she needed to season and cook it together.

“Searing everything on high heat is the secret for the best flavor, but it only works if you have a powerful stove. Otherwise, it’s best to simmer everything on low heat instead.”

She clearly knew what she was doing as she prepared the fried rice. And when she was done, it came out really well too.

Once they were done eating, they went back to the TV, and continued watching until it was eight in the night. By then, it was time to get to work, so Iris went to the respective room, and Mira waited while keeping watch outside.

Iris’ powers required a lot of focus, so Mira had to leave her alone during that time.

(Well, no better time to check this.)

They had been too busy with the tour, dinner, and TV so far, but now that she finally had some time for herself, she brought out the booklet that Alma had given her, which detailed all of the hidden security mechanisms.

“Let’s see here…”

Mira summoned her sofa in front of Iris’ work room, and sat on it to read.

First, there were the security systems, of which Iris only knew about half.

The entrance notifications and alarms were only the beginning, as the whole area was also equipped to verify who was in which room. But for safety reasons, there were no offensive or retaliatory systems, everything was designed to detect intruders as soon as possible.

Iris did not know how most of them worked or where they were installed, she only knew what to do in case something irregular was detected.

(That makes sense, with her powers, the less she knows the better.)

Her powers as the oracle allowed her to read someone’s mind to a certain extent, with the downside that the deeper that she went, the more the target would also learn about her.

So to avoid leaking how everything worked, various parts of the booklet were marked as “Secret from Iris.”

(Still, this really is packed with all of the newest technology.)

There was also the fact that Alma was treating this as an experimental site, so plenty of the devices there were not yet commonly available outside.

All of that was followed by a different type of information.

That included what Iris liked and disliked, her usual sleep and wake up time, and so on. Alma’s overprotective tendencies were also evident there.

All of the secret systems set in place made the oracle’s room more like a trap-ridden dungeon. Because of that, Mira also felt like she was exploring a dungeon as she tried to get her bearings.

The fact that there were no lethal traps might give the impression that it was not too bad, but everything was under such heavy surveillance that sneaking in undetected would be nigh impossible without the aid of someone like Worthramble.

On the other hand, if multiple units blindly stormed the place en masse, they would overwhelm the systems and some would make it through.

The traps would only serve to buy some time.

That was why Mira was there as a bodyguard, to stop that from happening. Her role was to protect Iris from any such blind suicide attack, and fully stop any intruders.

(Now…I wonder how they’ll react.)

Mira stashed away the booklet in her Item Box and glanced at the door of Iris’ work room.

They were expecting that August would learn about their plans once Iris used her powers to check what he was doing.

The most important part of that was obviously enough, the new bodyguard.

Before her, Iris’ bodyguard had been Noin the White Vault, one of Nirvana’s powerful Twelve Apostles.

No one had been able to bust through his defences, and there were plenty of stories from those who tried. He was largely known as the most powerful paladin of the whole continent.

Sadly, his protection had been rendered largely useless after August’s efforts to fight against the oracle’s abilities.

Now Iris had gained a phobia towards men. He would know for certain that his plan had worked, and that Mira was the new bodyguard to make up for that.

Alma had also made sure to make it seem like the bodyguard switch happened in a hurry.

Basically, she had talked to Iris as if she was trying to keep calm while clearly being disconcerted about the whole affair.

Her hope was for Iris to think it was a serious issue, but that they had just barely managed to find someone to keep her safe.

After all, August could only learn what Iris saw and believed, not the actual truth. And once he learned everything Iris had experienced, he would decide this was a good time to attack.

Nirvana’s undefeated hero was being replaced by a young adventurer girl whose power had gained popularity recently.

Since she was still considered an up-and-coming adventurer, even if she was strong, no one would expect her to stack up to a seasoned veteran. And given how the switch was done in a hurry, that would also make it easier to underestimate her.

But the truth was different.

That girl who had started to gain popularity was just a disguise for one of the Nine Wisemen, who were considered on par with the Twelve Apostles. Not only that, but she was the same person who had once shattered Noin’s ego.

(I’ll just have to catch whoever they send so that Kagura can get information out of them.)

Mira began setting up her own lookouts, using the location of the devices already present as reference, while Iris was busy doing her own work.

+++

# **340: Silent Watchers**

“Sorry for keeping you waiting!”

Around an hour after she entered the room, Iris was done and she came out.

“Welcome back, did anything happen?”

Iris was looking rather pale, which made Mira worried that the girl had pushed herself too much. In response, the fake smile on Iris’ face vanished, her whole body taking a disgusted look as she replied, “He’s such a degenerate!”

Apparently, August’s plan that had given Iris a phobia was still on-going.

Iris was clearly appalled and upset by all the lewdness she was forcefully exposed to, but she still pushed herself to complete her duty.

“You worked really hard, you did well.”

It was commendable that Iris kept going despite what she had to endure, which Mira made sure to state.

“…Mhm!”

Mira looked younger than Iris, but that mattered little when receiving a compliment, as Iris smiled with a bit of embarrassment.

The next step was to report on Iris’ new findings through the communications device, installed in the living room.

‘Thank you as always, Iris. Did it go well?’

Alma’s voice answered as soon as the call was placed, her voice tinged with worry.

Iris first glanced over at Mira before enthusiastically saying, “It did now that Mira is here!”

She had found the strength to smile despite the twisted ideas forced into her mind, allowing her to present her report effortlessly. In short, there were no major developments.

They also realized that anything they planned would be seen by Iris, so they were struggling to get anything done.

All of the connections and experience August had built up over the years were of no use to him anymore, and all the underground trading routes he managed were compromised.

It did not matter if there were things he kept secret or locked away. The moment he thought of using them, Iris would know, and Nirvana would ruin his efforts.

Even if he still had cards up his sleeve, for now all he could do was enrage Iris.

At the same time, not much could be gained from him anymore, but he would remain restrained for as long as Iris continued checking on him.

‘Thank you, Iris. You should take a well earned rest now. And Mira, thank you too, take care of Iris.’

Those were Alma’s final words once Iris finished her report. She sounded both proud and relieved that Iris could rest now.

It was already past ten in the night when the report wrapped up. Normally, that meant it was bedtime, but on the days that Iris had oracle work, she would first take a bath around that time. To wash off all sorts of things.

“Mira, you should come with me too!”

Iris’ eyes twinkled as she invited Mira. The bathroom there could easily fit two people, maybe even up to five. If anything, taking a bath together was the more efficient choice.

But Mira shook her head.

“Ah, sorry…I have something to do at the moment, I’ll take one later.”

Usually, Mira’s response would have been an instant yes, usually.

Things were just a little different here, there were simply way too many people nearby who knew Mira’s identity. There was Alma, Esmeralda, and the rest of the Twelve Apostles by extension, who all knew Mira was actually Danbulf.

Anyone else would not think twice seeing a beautiful girl like Mira entering a bath together with Iris. But Mira knew that Alma and the rest likely would see her as a pervert taking advantage of a young girl.

So despite the enticing invitation, Mira grit her teeth and forced herself to reject it.

“That’s too bad…”

Iris’ smile saddened a little.

She had lived secluded in that room for a long time, having no one else around, so she longed for the opportunity to share a bath with someone else. Being shot down like that left her heartbroken, even if she tried to smile through it.

“Ah, don’t feel sad! I should be done with everything tonight! So tomorrow it should work out!”

Just looking at Iris was enough to tell she had grown used to always being alone, which tugged on Mira’s heartstrings, who spoke without thinking.

Mira could resist temptation, but not guilt.

Those words also returned Iris’ smile. “No taking it back now!” She shouted as she hopped and skipped into the bathroom.

(Now then, what should I do to get out of this alive…)

Mira wasted no time to think up ways to explain her behavior once others found out she had bathed with Iris.

She could appeal to duty, claiming that it was the best way of keeping her safe at all times. Or she could rely on emotions, saying that she refused at first, but had no choice when Iris became depressed. There was also the combative option, saying there was no issue whatsoever with taking a bath together since Mira just saw Iris as her daughter.

And yet none of those options seemed like the best.

Amidst those thoughts, she suddenly thought of Mariana.

Was there any excuse she would accept if she found out that Mira was locked together with another girl, and even took baths together?

There was only so much Mira could think about, so in the end she gave up. Sometimes it was best to just let things happen and worry about them later, her mission was more important now.

“This balcony looks like a good first spot.”

Mira had not lied when she said she still had something to do, even if it helped her turn down Iris.

She wanted to perfect the room’s defenses, and she knew just how to do it. After pushing all other thoughts out of her mind, she began running around.

The booklet included detailed blueprints of the room as whole, which aided Mira in picking the best defensive spots.

First, she placed various Dark Knights all over the garden, with orders to restrain intruders.

Next, she focused on the more vital areas, like the living block, which was fully opened to the garden like an atrium. With no walls there, anyone who got to the garden would have no issue sneaking further inside.

To combat that, she placed Holy Knights on the balconies of every floor. And they were no regular Holy Knights either, they were imbued with the power of Worthramble, turning them invisible.

“Good, they shouldn’t get in the way like this.”

She nodded proud of herself as she looked at the balconies from the garden.

There were two reasons why she made the Holy Knights invisible. The first was out of consideration for Iris. Holy Knights were not gendered, but their appearance did resemble that of a burly powerful man, which could trigger Iris’ phobia.

The other reason was to keep them secret.

There was the danger of the enemy finding out about them through Iris, if she became aware of them, making their defense far less effective.

Since Iris was currently taking a bath alone, she would never know that Mira had been strengthening the defenses.

Summons filled all the areas that Mira felt needed more defenses.

Then again, this was the oracle’s room, within the imperial palace of Nirvana, protected by multiple layers of security. Alma also spared no expense when installing this room’s defenses. It was like an iron fortress impervious even to the most skilled spy.

Now that place was being guarded by Mira’s summons as well, so it was no exaggeration to say it would be impossible to break in.

“Let’s see how this goes for now.”

No matter how they got in, Mira would not let them lay a single finger on Iris. To ensure that, she went into her bedroom.

The only time someone was more defenseless than in the toilet, was while sleeping.

So Mira placed a special defensive summon in the bedroom.

The best guard that could stand watch all day without rest, with strength comparable to an A-rank adventurer. An Ashen Knight. Which was also concealed like the rest.

“Yes, now it’s perfect!”

Even if they were hidden, every important spot was protected now.

With that done, she set foot in the garden again. Not to reinforce it this time, as instead she took out her wagon. Specifically, she wanted to use the communications device inside the wagon. She wanted to report to Solomon, who surely was curious to know what she was up to.

‘Hello, this is Solomon of Arkite Castle.’

“Ah, it’s me, it’s me!”

‘Ahh, hey. How’s it going? Did you find her?’

“Yes, my senses are as sharp as ever…”

After their usual exchange, she began her report.

Mira had successfully tracked down Meilin with Alma’s help, finding she was staying with the Adams, a family of knights. She had also secured the help of a maid there, who would ensure the disguise was used.

“…So there’s no need to worry about her anymore. I’ve also asked to be told ahead of time when her matches will happen, so that I can double check myself.”

Mira had also asked Alma to know whenever Meilin would show up in the tournament, so that Mira could verify alongside the maid that Meilin was in disguise. That way, no one would know her identity, unless something extreme happened.

“Ahh, and before I forget…”

After telling him about Meilin, Mira then mentioned how she became the oracle’s bodyguard, at the behest of Alma and Esmeralda.

Solomon’s response was, ‘I see I see, that’s probably the main priority at the moment, yes.’

As it turned out, Alma had spoken with Solomon a few days prior, asking for advice on how to protect Iris now that she was afraid of men. That was when Solomon suggested that Mira would be the ideal pick, as she was already there for the tournament.

In the end, everything had been planned by Solomon.

‘Good luck as bodyguard. Maybe something good can come out from becoming friends with the oracle too.’

“I can’t believe you’re saying that…”

Mira could glean from Solomon’s words that he was looking forward to borrowing the oracle’s powers for his own plans eventually, which exasperated Mira.

That concluded Mira’s update for Solomon, so after hanging up, she quickly put her wagon away and returned to the room.

+++

# **341: A Regular Adventurer**

“Ahh, this is heaven…”

Mira’s turn in the bath came as soon as Iris was done with hers.

Alma’s overprotective nature with Iris was visible in the bathroom as well, which was furnished more luxuriously than even the most expensive inns. There was even a jacuzzi there, which Mira thoroughly enjoyed.

Once she had enough, she headed to the bedroom. By then it was past eleven, time for good girls to be in bed. So Mira expected Iris would be asleep, prompting her to be very careful when opening the door.

“Oh, you’re still awake?”

The lights were on, and Iris closed the book she was reading, smiling happily as she saw Mira was back.

“I don’t want to sleep just yet.”

She was brimming with energy, all because of Mira.

“Mira, I heard you’re an amazing adventurer, right? Tell me more about that. I want to know what kind of work adventurers do, and how they live.”

Saying that, she held up the book she was reading, which turned out to be a textbook for adventurers.

After meeting Mira and hearing her stories, Iris had gained an admiration for adventurers as a whole.

But the focus of her questions showed that she had a more mature interest, approaching the topic more carefully.

Unlike a lot of other people who just dreamed about that life, she was more realistic. That left a strong impression on Mira, who also realized that she could not answer that properly.

Iris was likely asking about the regular adventurers who made a living traveling everywhere, quite different from Mira, who worked under direct orders of Solomon. Her connections had allowed her to start off at rank C, and then she jumped to rank A after fighting Chimera Clauzen. Without having to formally accept a single request given out by the Union.

Her lifestyle also differed from most adventurers.

Solomon would fund her, for both military expenses and a personal allowance. Lately, she also spent the nights in her spirit mansion instead of camping in a tent.

The more she thought about it, the more she noticed how different her lifestyle was from those of adventurers, even if she herself longed for that life. Even her rank was hardly legitimate.

With all that considered, Mira could not really use her experience to answer Iris’ question.

But Iris did not know any of that, as she continued to stare at Mira with anticipation.

“Hmm… Well, there’s various ways for adventurers to make a living…”

Mira could not bring herself to say she did not know when faced by Iris’ anticipation, so instead she spoke of the general knowledge she had.

She was careful to not embellish or fill in the blanks she herself was ignorant to, only speaking in broad terms.

“Sometimes various adventurers work together, and whoever has the highest rank is chosen as leader…”

She also recalled the interactions she had with other adventurers, using them as a template.

It was true that she was a rank A adventurer on paper only. But she had experience working alongside other, more proper adventurers, so that gave her at least some knowledge.

Iris’ question was also a general one about adventurers, so it was best to give her a broad response. There was no reason for Mira to reveal her own lifestyle or her past work.

Then again, Mira still decided to put on airs acting like she had a wealth of experience, acting like she also did everything she spoke about.

She learned a few things when traveling together with Bruce as well, so she spoke at length about the types of requests available for adventurers.

All the requests she had actually seen were meant for lower ranked adventurers, but as Iris knew hardly anything about them, she reacted with excitement to everything.

“…And that’s about it. It’s a world with large rewards, but also large risks.”

There were many sides to being an adventurer, and only a few were fun and exciting. It was not a line of work to earn a living, but to find something worth living for.

After relating everything she knew about adventurers, Mira wrapped things up with her own view of that lifestyle.

“That sounds incredibly cool!”

Her friends would call her out if they heard her say that, but Iris was the only person there, who admired Mira as a rank A adventurer.

So Mira’s words had a strong effect on the girl, whose bright smile took a more serious appearance as she muttered, “I wonder if I’ll find something like that too.”

Their conversation went on for so long that soon it would be midnight, and Mira could not repress her yawns anymore. While Iris was still full of energy.

“Can you also tell me about the strongest monster you’ve fought?”

Her curiosity was far from satiated.

(I was hoping she would fall asleep eventually, but it seems I’ll be the first one…)

Mira had noticed that she was getting sleepy faster ever since she turned into a girl. Being reminded of that, she replied, “Let’s leave that for tomorrow, it’s too late now,” and flipped the lightswitch. As the room was shrouded in darkness, she let out another yawn and slipped into her bed.

“Alright…”

Iris still wanted to hear more stories, so she sounded a bit let down.

Ideally, Mira also wanted to gloat about her accomplishments, but she could hardly keep her eyes open anymore.

“There’s always tomorrow and the days after that. This is barely my first day here.”

Mira pointed out that they would have plenty of time to talk in the future, which cheered up Iris as she happily said, “You’re right. I can’t wait for tomorrow!”

“The sooner we sleep, the faster we’ll wake up!”

A rustling sound indicated Iris had also gotten in her bed, deciding to sleep without complaining more.

(I have a long road ahead of me.)

Mira closed her eyes, thinking of stories she could tell in the future for only a bit, as she fell asleep much faster than Iris.

---

Far away in a certain small room.

There was a man sitting imposingly on a fancy chair. He was August, one of the highest members of Ira Muerte.

‘What gave you the idea of calling us? Do you understand the position you’re in?’

‘Our hands are already full now that Trulli is being hunted down. I’ll make you pay if you’re just wasting our time.’

Two irritated voices came from the device on a nearby table, who seemed fed up because of someone called Trulli.

“Yes, I know. I’m not that dense. Trulli’s hands are also tied because I’m being pinned down by Nirvana’s oracle, and I’m sorry for that.”

He apologized with an indifferent attitude, but there was a soft smile on his face.

That Trulli they were talking about was another of the top members of Ira Muerte. He was mainly in charge of Ira Muerte’s slave trade, but after August lost control of their trading routes, and with Trulli’s merchandise being on a timer, he had no choice but to attempt to secure his own trading routes.

That was not something he was used to doing, so it did not take long after he left his safehouse that he fell in a police trap.

‘How much did you know about that? From what we’ve seen, that trap was really elaborate, almost like they knew everything. You didn’t leak anything about that, did you?’

“How could I? You should know better than anyone that I’m entirely out of the loop now. You didn’t tell me anything, and neither did Trulli. I don’t know anything about his plans or how they failed.”

August replied with a calm voice to the accusations. He did not know any of Trulli’s plans. And since he did not know that, Nirvana’s oracle would not have been able to know either.

“If they really knew what he was doing, then there’s a leak somewhere else. Then again, I can’t help with that since I know nothing new.”

In short, August was blaming Trulli for not being careful enough and falling for the ambush.

‘That doesn’t change the fact that this all happened because of you. All of this could’ve been avoided if you just hadn’t let Nirvana put you on a leash.’

‘Yes, we’ve helped you out in the past whenever we could, only for you to ruin everything. Don’t act like this doesn’t concern you.’

“Okay okay, I already said I’m sorry. And it’s not fair that they have someone with that kind of power. I would’ve been more careful if I knew.”

The two would constantly blame him whenever they found an opening, and August apologized every time, though in person he did not look apologetic at all, and was clearly fed up.

“Anyway, moving on. There’s a good reason why I’ve called you. I might have found a solution for the situation I’m in…”

August moved the conversation before the two could start complaining about him again.

The oracle’s power revealed anything August was planning, but that came at the cost of revealing what the oracle knew as well, giving August a glimpse into what was happening in Nirvana.

“…So it’s safe to say that my plan was successful and they changed the oracle’s bodyguard. The White Vault is gone, replaced by that new Spirit Queen adventurer.”

Even if she was a powerful adventurer, August claimed that she would be much easier to deal with than one of the monstrous Twelve Apostles.

After enduring this for so long, there was finally an opening on the oracle’s side. August would not let that go to waste, and he wanted to move past his previous failures.

‘Now that’s interesting. I never thought that freaky plan of yours would work, and they downgraded from an Apostle to an adventurer. I guess I can forgive you for calling us like this.’

The first of the pair agreed with August’s assessment. Noin’s defense was largely considered impregnable, with no one alive being able to land a single hit on him, so anyone else would be an easier target.

“We finally have our chance, don’t you think? Garroba?”

August successfully diverted their attention, and wanting to carry that momentum he asked for the opinion of the third member in their conversation.

Garroba, another high ranking member of Ira Muerte, and the leader of their infiltration and assassination unit.

‘The Spirit Queen… I believe she was one of the adventurers that stood out during the Chimera incident. Still, I guess we’ll have a better chance with her.’

It took him a while to reply, a pensive tone to his voice. Garroba was also of the mind that an adventurer was a better opponent than one of the Twelve Apostles.

“See? Anyway, I’ll let you guys decide what to do with this information, as usual. If you get rid of the oracle for me, I promise to make up for all the idle time I’ve had.”

The following discussion on how to use that information was not for August’s ears, so he stood up from the chair. If he heard their plan, the oracle would also find out soon enough.

All he could do was to share the information he gained.

“Well then, I’ll let you know if I find out anything more.”

With those parting words, August left the room. But he did not hang up the call, as that device was used exclusively for meetings amongst leaders, and was always connected.

So even with August gone, the other two voices continued to ring through it.

‘So what do you make of this? Security might be more lax, but we still haven’t been able to pinpoint the oracle’s location whatsoever.’

‘That’s one thing, yes. Something else is bothering me though.’

‘Oh? Did you notice something?’

‘The Spirit Queen. Is she really just a regular adventurer? I get she’s really skilled, but is that really all it takes to become a replacement for one of the Twelve Apostles?’

The Twelve Apostles were Nirvana’s strongest force, so Garroba found it curious that instead of picking another Apostle, they chose the Spirit Queen, a mere adventurer who just so happened to be gaining popularity.

‘Now that you mention it, hmm… There were some rumors that they already had some sort of connection, so maybe that’s why? Or maybe they’re trying to gain the trust of spirits as well.’

That man only knew about the Spirit Queen through hearsay.

Random booms in popularity for certain adventurers were not an uncommon thing. The Spirit Queen had also made an impactful appearance with the Spirit King, so her popularity was understandable.

And being able to get the Spirit King as an ally was also a good enough reason to pick her over another Apostle. At least that was the man’s line of thought. But Garroba was still not fully convinced yet.

‘The Spirit King… Hmm, having to fight spirits could get annoying, true. But something still feels off.’

Saying that, he elaborated on that point. While everyone spoke about the Spirit King, he had only been in the picture once.

‘Oh right… Now that I think about it, he only showed up in Sentopolly that one time. I’ve never heard of her using the Spirit King’s power again.’

As far as they knew, the Spirit King had never shown himself again. Some people were theorizing that she had never been able to summon the Spirit King to begin with.

Maybe it had all been an act. A show put together by the spirits there, pretending to be the Spirit King. Or the other possibility was that they just had a different connection, and the Spirit King made an exception to show up there himself.

‘There’s too much we don’t know. I think it’d be best to look more into this Spirit Queen before we plan anything.’

Someone like Nirvana’s empress would also know about all those rumors and theories, and despite so many doubts, she had chosen the Spirit Queen over the Apostles. Garroba could not help it but find that odd.

What kind of adventurer was she? How strong was she really? What was her connection to the Spirit King? Those were all questions Garroba wanted to clear up first, planning how to take down the oracle would come later.

‘Does that sound good?’

‘Yes, I’m down for that. It’s that empress we’re talking about, you never know what she’s planning. We should be as cautious as possible.’

The man continued, ‘I’ll check with my usual connections,’ and left his seat, followed by fading footsteps and a door being closed shut.

‘That’s a wrap then. I’ll see myself out as well.’

Even as everyone else left, Garroba still spoke into the device before leaving.

There was no response, and soon his leaving footsteps also faded into silence.

+++

# **342: TV Watchparty**

“Wake up Grandpa, it’s morning already! How much longer are you going to sleep?”

The morning after Mira began working as the oracle Iris’ bodyguard, she was shaken awake, and she let out a groan as her half-asleep eyes opened to see who was bothering her.

“Oh, Alma…hrngghhh… Good morning.”

Sitting up to stretch, she greeted Alma before staring blankly into space, a part of her clearly still in dreamland.

“Good morning. And don’t try to sleep again.”

Alma pulled the sheets away and took hold of Mira, who was trying to lay down again.

“Okay let’s get you in the shower, that should wake you up.”

Saying that, she dragged Mira from the bedroom to the bathroom.

“When you’re done, come down to the room where we ate yesterday. I’m getting breakfast ready.”

Alma said that after throwing Mira into the changing room, leaving to go downstairs. She was busy as usual.

“Hmm…”

Since she had stayed up late the night before, Mira was still drowsy, and mindlessly followed what she was told, ending up inside the shower. The comforting warm water that rained over her was perfect to wake up.

“Ah… It’s already morning.”

Finally fully awake, she was able to complete her usual morning routine without issue.

After breakfast with Alma and Iris in the kitchen and dining room, they spent some time sharing a cup of tea.

Once again, they talked about various things. Most of it was of little importance, which in a way made the time they spent together all the more dear. Alma and Iris looked especially at ease as they spoke.

Sadly, that could not go on forever, so around ten minutes later, things played out very similarly to the previous day. Esmeralda showed up, ready to drag Alma away to the duties she had been abandoning.

“She seems pretty busy so early on.”

As Alma left the room, Mira began to ponder. At first glance, it appeared like Alma went there to avoid working, but maybe it was mainly to see Iris.

Just looking at the girl proved that.

Iris had no choice but to remain shut away in this place, doing her work as oracle. Being in such a lonesome position would leave anyone distraught, but Alma’s efforts allowed Iris to remain smiling.

It was also clear from these two days that Alma went to see Iris with quite a lot of frequency.

So to make Alma’s efforts count, and to protect Iris’ smile, Mira would also do her best. At least mentally, it would take some time before anything happened.

The assassins she had discovered two days prior had not determined Iris’ position yet, so going from that to invading her room would take time.

On top of that, there were all the defensive systems Alma had installed, and Mira’s summons standing guard. As long as they remained in the room, Iris would be safe.

Mira’s time for action would come later on. After all, that was the reason why she had come to replace Noin, for the promised visit to the tournament.

Iris had been looking forward to being there in person, but she needed a bodyguard, and Noin could no longer do that due to her fear of men. When that happened, the risk of her leaving the room was deemed too high, and the visit was called off.

Until Mira showed up.

Things had been quite the tangled mess behind the scenes, but thanks to Alma, Iris remained cheerful through it all.

“Ah, the next event is about to start…”

Iris blurted that after looking at the time, before adding, “Come watch too, Mira!” before darting out of the dining room.

“And someone else is full of energy so early on too.”

Mira muttered to herself as she followed Iris, wondering what event she was referring to.

That turned out to be the pre-show events being carried out in the tournament grounds. There was quite a long lineup of smaller events scheduled, which the whole city was looking forward to even before the main tournament.

Iris had been watching those events as well, thanks to the Magic TV in the living room.

This was her first time doing so together with someone else though, she was really excited to get things ready.

She skillfully tuned in to the right channel, and then swiftly placed various snacks and drinks on the table. It took almost no time for the perfect watching environment to be created.

(This really brings me back to those weekends…)

Mira was thinking about her time in modern Japan, where she would do something very similar to watch movies. At the same time, the speed at which Iris set everything up terrified Mira.

(We really need to deal with Ira Muerte as soon as possible so Iris can learn to live a proper life outside…)

At this rate, Iris would become a shut in who just watched TV all the time. Mira was already seeing the early signs of that, so she hoped that Ira Muerte could be dealt with soon to put an end to this lifestyle.

“Mira, Mira, sit here!”

Those worries circled around in Mira’s mind as Iris sat down on the couch and called Mira to sit next to her.

Iris had also placed a pile of snacks and drinks for Mira, being really excited to have someone to watch TV with.

“Okay.”

Mira replied and sat down next to Iris.

A soft couch, the best snacks and drinks in the empire, and a TV. That alone made Mira excited, just as the event began and the announcer’s greetings were passed through the Magic TV.

“Hmm…I wonder what’s going to happen.”

She could see thirty two participants on stage, and a woman as the announcer.

The whole stage was displayed, so it was a bit hard to tell the faces of any person there, but it was clear that the participants were of all ages, with both children and adults present, and both males and females.

A tournament bracket was also displayed behind them, so it was still some sort of competition, despite the large disparities amongst participants.

Mira could only wonder what kind of event that was.

The answer for all that came from Iris, before it became clear on the TV.

“Today they’re playing the final tournament of Legend of Astelia on stage. I can’t wait to see what will happen!”

After that, Iris began to mention who she believed would win the tournament. As it turned out, she had memorized the entire event schedule.

Mira was impressed by that, but also muttered with surprise, “So the finals were here.”

Legend of Astelia was a card game that had become popular across the continent.

It had not been long since Mira also watched a qualifier game play out, where a woman won by using Danbulf’s card. That prompted Mira to search for the woman she had seen, but the event was already moving to the first match, so she could no longer look at all the participants.

Iris did not only know about the game, but was quite into playing as well, and she would often play with Alma and Esmeralda as well. That was another reason why she was so excited to watch. Maybe she could learn something she could apply to her own deck.

Esmeralda’s deck tended to have various cards with good synergy, while Alma tackled every issue throwing money at it, so she mostly had high value cards.

And then the first match of the Legend of Astelia Final Tournament began.

The large display switched from the tournament bracket to a direct feed of the playing table, allowing Iris and Mira to watch clearly through the Magic TV screen as well.

Eventually, the third match came around. This time it was a Paladin player against a Death Knight player, which was a really exciting match that kept Iris at the edge of her seat.

“That’s incredible! I didn’t know you could do that!”

“Ohh they turned things around again. This match is far from over then.”

By then, Mira was also fully immersed in the match, attentively watching every play.

She had learned the basic rules during the first match she watched before, so now she was also able to follow what was happening. Only the specific card effects were still a bit of a mystery to her.

Thankfully, every time she asked, “What did they just do?” Iris would be able to give a perfect explanation.

“Oh, I think that settles it.”

“This is a really tight spot! But if that card is played then it might keep going…”

Eventually, the Paladin player was pushed into a corner, and Mira was sure that this was the end of the match, but Iris could still see a way out. There was a specific card in the Paladin deck that could turn things around once more.

The player took a card from the stack, then remained silent in thought for a while. The card had not been pulled.

And then cards began getting shuffled around rapidly, combining various card and unit effects, until the player finally reached the card that Iris had mentioned.

“What just happened! Somehow, the table was turned around once more!”

“That was so cool, too cool! I would’ve never thought of doing that to pull the card!”

It was not even the final match but the crowd could not be more excited by it all, and that extended to Mira and Iris.

Not long after that the match was over. The Paladin player’s last switchup had decided the match and emerged victorious, and the audience erupted with applause for both players.

“The first two matches were fun, but this one was the best.”

“I’ve never seen such a sequence of counterattack after counterattack.”

The two continued to talk during the break before the next match, still discussing the third match. Iris had plenty of new ideas, and Mira was starting to think of building her own deck as well.

They were eventually interrupted by a noise that resembled wind chimes.

“Hm? What’s that noise?”

Over at the balcony, there were no wind chimes hung up, not to mention that it sounded like the noise came from within the room, where there was no wind. But before long, the origin of that sound became clear.

“I’m going!”

As if someone had summoned her, Iris stood up and walked over to a corner of the room.

That sound had been the ringing of a communications device.

This one looked different from the one in Mira’s wagons, having all sorts of additional switches attached making it look more complicated, but Iris swiftly operated it, showing how used she was to it.

“Iris here!”

After flipping various switches, Iris finally pulled a lever and picked up.

‘Hey, I’m Alma. Tell me, is Mira somewhere nearby?’

Alma’s voice came out from the receiver. And from her words, it was safe to assume she had something to discuss with Mira.

Wondering if it had anything to do with their preparations from the previous day, Mira got up to answer, but Iris was faster.

“Yup! We’re watching the Astelia finals together!”

Her enthusiasm for watching TV with someone else was obvious from her excited voice.

‘Ah, I forgot. That was today.’

Meanwhile, Alma sounded shocked. She was also interested in the card game, so she was curious about the tournament as well. ‘How many matches did they already play? Did Friede play yet?’ She asked soon after, unable to stop her curiosity.

“The fourth match is just about to start. Friede will play the match after the next one.”

‘Gotcha, so it’ll take a bit longer. He’s something like Nirvana’s representative, so I really hope he wins!’

“I hope so too!”

That led to the two discussing the card game tournament further, as they not only enjoyed the game, but the player Friede was also their regional champion who had remained in the competition, and they wanted to see him succeed.

The two were deeply aware of Friede’s personal deck and playstyle, almost like they knew him in person.

Mira had also been able to glean from that conversation that Friede had always stood out during the qualifying matches as well, which Iris had also watched through the Magic TV.

‘Did you say they only played three matches so far? I would’ve expected them to be in the fifth match by now.’

Alma also took note of the time since the scheduled start of the tournament, once they were done talking about Friede.

Usually games of Legend of Astelia took half an hour, and it had been two hours since the event started.

“Ah, that’s because the third match was really crazy. I still can’t believe what happened.”

‘That’s a lot of praise from you. What happened in that game?’

“There were reversals after reversals! And I never thought that you could use that card in that position, it was a lot!”

‘Oh? What card did they use? What did they do?!’

“Heheheh, that’s a secret! I’ll use it the next time we play.”

‘Hey! That’s not fair!’

Just when it seemed like they were done, the two got fully engaged in their conversation again.

As usual, the best topic of conversation was a mutual interest or hobby, and the two would not run out of things to say.

“Helloooooo, did you forget about meee? I thought you wanted to talk.”

As the two discussed fun ideas for new decks, when new card packs would be sold, the possibility of Cecilia getting her own card soon, and so on, Mira raised her voice and interrupted them. After all, the call had been for her.

‘…Ah, I forgot!’

Alma had gotten so carried away talking with Iris that she was clearly startled when Mira reminded her. The conversation with Iris was postponed, and she went back to the main reason for the call.

‘Umm, _ahem_, so the thing we discussed yesterday went way faster than we thought. Apparently they’re in the waiting room right now, so you can go check on them and pick it up.’

Alma’s voice was unusually vague, hardly mentioning anything specific, since she was aware that the enemy could end up learning of their plans through Iris. That much was obvious to Mira, and she also picked up on what Alma meant.

(That’s the Kagura I know, she already sent it.)

The thing from yesterday and picking up clearly meant that Piisuke had arrived at the Fifty Bells Branch, and that the director Claus had brought the shikigami to the palace.

“I understand.”

When Mira replied, Alma casually said, ‘Thank you!’ like she had just asked someone to pick up a delivery for her. That was probably another way to not let Iris know how important this was.

‘And Iris, please tell me how the tournament went during dinner tonight, okay?’

“Okay!”

With that final exchange, Alma hung up. At the same time, the Magic TV became more audible.

The break was over and the fourth match was starting.

It was hard to tell the players’ faces apart from the distant viewpoint, but their height difference was striking.

It was a young boy against a grown man. If this was a fighting tournament, the match would be over in seconds, but in a card game, the two stood on equal ground. And somehow, it felt natural to want to root for the young boy to win.

But Mira had no time to stay and watch that match.

+++

# **343: Good tidings**

“I’ll be going for a bit then.”

Mira asked Iris to also tell her the result of the match when she returned, just like Alma did, and then stood up to leave. Iris replied with a cheerful, “Take care!” But Mira did not miss the sudden pang of loneliness that overtook Iris’ eyes right after.

(Oh right, she’ll be all alone again once I leave…)

The way Iris spoke, always ready to explain anything that happened, showed that she truly enjoyed watching TV with someone else, and now she was trying to push those feelings away.

All to not make Mira worry.

That made Mira want to alleviate the loneliness somehow, until she came to a solution.

“Now that I think about it, I’m your bodyguard so I shouldn’t be leaving just like that. I’ll leave this fellow here to protect you in my stead until my return.”

There were already more than a dozen Holy Knights and Dark Knights standing guard, on top of the Ashen Knight in the room, keeping Iris completely safe. But Mira still felt the need of saying that as she activated a summon, all to keep Iris company.

A magic circle spread out, and with a heroic stride, the First Lieutenant Cait Sith emerged from it. It really felt like he had rehearsed how to make the perfect entrance as a summon.

“I’m but a wandering bodyguard. Would you like to meownploy me? If you can afford meow that is.”

His attitude was a bit more coolheaded than usual, which sadly clashed with the slightly oversized black suit and mismatched sunglasses he wore.

Behind him the sign also read [Always safe with MeowLSOK]. This time he was playing the character of a professional bodyguard.

“Here, I’ll pay you in advance.”

Saying that, Mira threw him a slice of mountain tuna from her Item Box.

“Meohoow! Now we’re in business!”

He had not been expecting to actually be paid, so his eyes twinkled as he pounced on the slice of fish. Once he was done eating, he stood up with pride announcing, “I won’t let anyone lay a single finger on you now.”

“A talking cat! He’s so cuteee!”

He was trying his best to appear cool and dashing, but no matter what he did, he would never look that way. Just like Iris only saw him as an embodiment of cuteness.

“Can I pet you?”

Iris clasped and released her hands as she waddled closer to the First Lieutenant, filled with desire.

Meanwhile, the First Lieutenant’s attempt to remain cool and collected began to falter when faced with such a direct proposition, eventually slumping his shoulders and answering, “If it’s just a little…you can.”

The decision between staying in character or giving in to Iris’ request ended up with him going for the latter option.

“You’re so cuteeee! And fluffyyyyy!”

As soon as he gave permission, Iris darted forward and began petting the First Lieutenant all over.

Mira had relied on the idea that there was no girl who disliked small animals, and it paid off. Her smile as she petted the First Lieutenant was pure and free of worry, also making Mira smile.

“Well then, First Lieutenant. I’m leaving her in your paws.”

Mira no longer had to worry about Iris being lonely, and if anything were to happen, the First Lieutenant would be able to buy time until Mira got back as well. They were not in a battlefield or somewhere dangerous, so Iris would be safe.

“You can count on meow!”

The First Lieutenant replied with determination, which did not really do much for him as Iris hugged him.

After leaving Iris and the First Lieutenant in the room, Mira headed out to the waiting room where Claus was.

“Oh, Mira, where are you going?”

“Just running an errand for the empress.”

After reaching the break room at the end of the corridor leading out of the oracle’s room, she encountered some guards who were resting there.

She spoke for a bit with one of them, who was no average guard. She had seen his face alongside various others in the booklet Alma gave her, as well as a description of the place.

The break room was just a front, with its true purpose being a place to guard the entrance to the oracle’s room.

At first glance, it just looked like the guards were taking a break there, but on closer examination, it was clear that everyone there was no average person.

If the booklet was right, then everyone there was at least a commander, which meant their power was above rank A adventurers, and they were permanently stationed in that room while just pretending to rest.

“I’ll only be gone for a bit, so don’t worry.”

There were presently three guards there, who appeared to be relaxing, while still being in positions where they could draw their swords at a moment’s notice. Even if Mira was not planning on doing anything, just being there made her straighten her back and walk properly.

The entrance to the room was also under heavy surveillance. But Mira was not intimidated, speaking to them with a casual tone.

“I understand. Take care.”

One of them replied, and the other two nodded silently. The three of them kept looking at her as she left and headed to the waiting room.

“…I got lost.”

Fifteen minutes passed after she left the oracle’s room.

She had been wandering through the palace the entire time, only to realize that the place she initially believed was the waiting room was the audience hall, and she no longer knew her way around.

If she could only bring herself to admit she was lost, she could have asked any of the servants she passed by for directions, and stopped wasting time.

But she stubbornly believed her half baked knowledge was enough, so she kept taking random turns, thinking that surely she was on the right path this time, only to reach more dead ends.

At first, she had walked with determination and pride, but as time went on, she gradually lost that confidence, until she just looked like a young girl who went to a big company to bring her father something he forgot at home.

Eventually, that allowed a female knight to take notice of Mira’s unsure manner of walking, and after making contact, she brought Mira to the waiting room.

“Sorry for troubling you, but thank you.”

“This palace is huge, so don’t mention it. It’s the least I could do for a guest.”

After thanking the female knight, Mira hurried to get inside the waiting room, having wasted so much time to get there.

And then…

“Cherry Rose requires a lot of care when drying, as the temperature and humidity of the air can affect its taste and aroma.”

“That explains it. I was wondering why it came out differently all the time.”

Claus was inside the waiting room, together with a maid of the palace.

(They seem lost in their conversation.)

The table was covered with tea cups, way more than one would expect to be offered to a guest. Judging by their conversation, they were discussing the various herbal teas in the cups.

Both of them were so passionate and into the conversation that they did not notice Mira’s arrival.

(What is this I see? They’re getting along so well!)

One of them was Claus, a burly man with looks that could make a child cry. The other was a pretty maid, with a relaxing aura to herself.

Having intruded on them like that, Mira silently retreated to the cover of a shelf, spying on them.

“You prepared this Yellowline Grass incredibly well. It’s quite difficult to get this color.”

“My grandmother taught me how to prepare it. I’m really proud of it myself. Thank you.”

Claus’ praise made the maid smile with a hint of embarrassment, clearly at ease in his presence. Maybe there were so many other strong men in the palace that she was not intimidated by him.

He also noticed that, as he appeared even more embarrassed than her.

(Is this what I think it is?! Were they destined to meet here?! There has to be a spark here!)

Both of them were invested in their conversation, constantly looking at each other as well. And to top it all off, Mira could hear the echoes of Martel’s happy shrieks in her mind.

The tea served there had been the catalyst for that entire conversation, at least judging by what they said now.

Claus was the director of the Fifty Bells Branch, turned manager of Everforest Garden, a store that sold the best products from the forest, making him very knowledgeable about herbs.

That knowledge meshed together with the tea the maid served, leading to the current situation.

(And this is all thanks to me getting lo… Thanks to me taking a detour.)

Their conversation would have been cut short much earlier if Mira had arrived on time, so she was convinced that she was the one responsible for this development.

Feeling like she was some sort of cupid, she silently left the room, then knocked loudly on the door and stepped back in.

“I’m sorry for taking so long, I accidentally went to the wrong place, so I had to take a detour.”

The maid quickly moved to the side, remaining silent, and Claus stood up looking faintly disappointed, as Mira acted like she had just arrived.

“That’s understandable, this is a really big palace after all.”

Claus replied as Mira approached, and the maid quickly put away all the tea cups from the table.

Mira pretended not to notice all of the cups, adding, “And it has a really weird layout too, so you better take care when leaving. Or maybe you could ask her to show you the way?” and looked at the maid.

Still clinging to her made up role of cupid, she tried to find any reason to bring the two together, even if it was a little forceful.

“That…is a good idea. I just kept looking at everything since it’s my first time here that I hardly paid attention to the path I took. I’d appreciate some help when leaving.”

Claus also mentioned how he believed he could get lost, so he more than happily accepted Mira’s suggestion.

“Of course, I’ll be ready when the time comes then.”

The maid had also heard everything, and readily agreed, adding, “I’ll leave you to it now,” leaving only two cups on the table, for Mira and Claus, and leaving with the rest. All of her actions were swift, her feet almost gliding on the ground as she left elegantly.

(She also seems to be into him, my cupid abilities are so good too!!)

“So, did you bring the thing?”

Mira felt quite proud of herself for bringing them together, but pretended not to notice a thing as she changed topics.

“It’s over here…”

Claus’ eyes followed the maid for a little while before hurrying to pick up a bag he had left next to his seat, producing a large box from within.

“That was such a curious experience. First, it said it would become easier to carry, and then it shrunk all of a sudden.”

He related what happened when Kagura’s shikigami Piisuke arrived, as the shikigami spoke to them before quickly shrinking to the size of a sparrow.

“Ohh, ohhh, it’s been a while since this happened.”

Piisuke let out a short chirp before flapping its wings to make a beeline to Mira’s head, almost like that was its designated sitting spot.

“Alright, delivery confirmed. And thank you again for taking the trouble of coming all this way.”

“Don’t mention it, it was no bother at all. If anything I appreciate the opportunity to go outside for once.”

Claus appeared just as grateful as Mira. His daily routine left him shut away in his office filing paperwork all day long, as his appearance often spooked clients. Being able to get some fresh air and spend time outside was a welcome change.

And Mira was convinced that he was also glad that he had met that maid from earlier.

“Hmm, that’s good to hear then.”

Mira’s ego inflated even more, as she had essentially granted them the opportunity to meet, and to establish a connection. She would also continue cheering them on while watching from afar.

“I must head back now, but as you mentioned, it’s not often that you get to spend time outside, so try to make the best of it that you can. It’s getting rather late too, so maybe you could have lunch here as well?”

Mira emptied her herbal tea cup, took a deep breath, and once again tried to push those two together, essentially hinting at the possibility of a lunch date.

“Well… Yes, I might as well do that since I’m here.”

It was hard to tell whether he realized what Mira was doing, but he did seem pleased with the idea. Either way, the rest would be in his hands, so Mira said a quick good bye and headed out the waiting room.

The maid was waiting right outside, so Mira told her, “Please look after him,” once again gently nudging them together, and then headed to the office where Alma waited for her.

+++

# **344: Alma and Kagura**

“Sorry for keeping you waiting, Alma. I brought Piisuke.”

In Alma’s office, Mira sat down on the couch while telling her that.

Alma had been waiting for that all morning, so she quickly threw her papers aside and ran up to Mira.

“Thank you, Grandpa. So… Where is…Piisuke?”

Once close, Alma tilted her head in confusion.

She knew what Piisuke looked like, a brilliant and elegant suzaku, with a very particular look, which proved just how skilled of an onmyoji master Kagura was. Alma could recognize it instantly, but there was no such bird near Mira.

Her eyes moved around aimlessly, eventually noticing Mira’s head.

“Huh? Wait, is that…”

A small and plump red sparrow was sitting on Mira’s head, which had not been there when Alma saw Mira earlier in the morning. Trying to understand what she was seeing, she moved closer.

‘Alma, it’s nice to see you again!’ a voice suddenly came from Piisuke.

Alma yelped as she jumped back, startled by that voice. The last thing she had been expecting was to hear the bird speak.

“So yes, this is Piisuke, and that was Kagura speaking through Piisuke.”

Smiling teasingly, Mira lowered Piisuke to the sofa, where the shikigami began to shake a little and then grew to its full suzaku appearance.

“Woah, that shocked me… I didn’t know onmyoji masters could do this too.”

There was no doubt left that this was Piisuke, looking like a completely different entity to the small bird from earlier. And that was not the end of the surprises, as Piisuke began to glow.

“Huh? What’s happening now?!”

Alma’s eyes filled with anticipation as she watched. The light became so bright that it blinded them for a moment, and when they could see again, Kagura was standing there, her hands up in the air as she exclaimed, “Ta-da!”

“Ah, Kagura! I’ve missed you so much!”

Seeing an old friend was far more impactful than the transformation, as Alma lunged forward, tackling Kagura.

“Whawe?! Wait!”

That resulted with both of them falling down violently on the couch, which did not bother or stop Alma in the slightest as she tightly embraced Kagura.

It did not take long after that for Kagura to give up on resisting, as there was little she could do with Alma straddling her from above.

“Oh yes…that’s nice, really nice.”

Watching the close relationship between two girls was truly a sight to behold, as Mira grinned watching their reencounter.

---

“…And that’s where your help would come in handy, Kagura. Can you help us?”

Once Alma calmed down, they explained the situation to Kagura.

Alma mentioned the large criminal organization Ira Muerte, as well as Jorg, the member they had captured, and how they had failed to get any usable information out of him no matter what they tried.

“I was wondering what Grandpa’s message was about when I heard it, now it all makes sense. Ira Muerte is a name I’ve heard a few times too, my spies mentioned they had some involvement with Chimera as well.”

With everyone on the same page, Kagura replied with interest, and a bit of intrigue.
